893:### 4.10 Cost ledger row shapes (`subscription_mediated`, `sandbox_compute`)
894:
895:Both are rows in the existing `llm_requests` table (or whatever the canonical cost-ledger table is â€” the spec uses `llm_requests` as the working name per the agent's extraction). Producer in this spec: the cost-writer hook called from the finaliser path. Consumer: existing usage views and rollups.
896:
897:**`subscription_mediated` row** (zero-cost, one per `operator_session`-mode chain link):
898:
899:```json
900:{
901:  "id": "<uuid>",
902:  "source_type": "subscription_mediated",
903:  "agent_run_id": "9e1f3b88-...",
904:  "operator_run_id": "<chain-link-uuid>",
905:  "organisation_id": "<org-uuid>",
906:  "subaccount_id": "<sub-uuid>",
907:  "chain_seq": 3,
908:  "vendor_session_id": "opv1-9bf3c0...",
909:  "credential_mode": "operator_session",
910:  "plan_tier": "plus",
911:  "step_count": 84,
912:  "input_tokens": 0,
913:  "output_tokens": 0,
914:  "cost_cents": 0,
915:  "created_at": "2026-05-12T16:01:43Z"
916:}
917:```
918:
919:**`sandbox_compute` row** (real spend, one per chain link):
920:
921:```json
922:{
923:  "id": "<uuid>",
924:  "source_type": "sandbox_compute",
925:  "agent_run_id": "9e1f3b88-...",
926:  "operator_run_id": "<chain-link-uuid>",
927:  "organisation_id": "<org-uuid>",
928:  "subaccount_id": "<sub-uuid>",
929:  "vcpu_seconds": 7200,
930:  "wall_clock_ms": 7192000,
931:  "peak_memory_bytes": 1_073_741_824,
932:  "cost_cents": 73,
933:  "created_at": "2026-05-12T16:01:43Z"
934:}
935:```
936:
937:**New typed columns vs `metadata` jsonb.** Only two columns are added to `llm_requests` by this spec: `operator_run_id` (nullable; references `operator_runs(id)`) and `boundary` (nullable; the discriminator the cost-writer keys on â€” currently the single value `'chain_link'`). The other operator-specific fields in the example rows above (`chain_seq`, `vendor_session_id`, `credential_mode`, `plan_tier`, `step_count`, `vcpu_seconds`, `wall_clock_ms`, `peak_memory_bytes`) are written into the existing `llm_requests.metadata` jsonb column, NOT as new typed columns. The cost-writer's JSON shape is named in `operatorCostWriterPure.ts` (Â§ 5.1). Migration `0331` also adds the covering index `(operator_run_id)` for cost-writer idempotency lookups and the partial UNIQUE `(operator_run_id, source_type, boundary)`.
938:
939:### 4.11 Source-of-truth precedence
940:
941:Where the same fact has more than one representation, the read path is:
942:
943:| Fact | Representations | Read priority |
944:|---|---|---|
945:| Chain-link terminal status | `operator_runs.status`, `'operator-session.chain_link_*'` event, finaliser log | `operator_runs.status` > event > log |
946:| Task terminal status | `agent_runs.status`, `'operator-session.task_*'` event, finaliser log | `agent_runs.status` > event > log |
947:| Chain-link wall-clock minutes | `(completed_at - started_at)`, the `sandbox_compute` ledger row's `wall_clock_ms` | DB timestamps win (per Â§ 3.17 item 4 DB-anchored discipline) |
948:| Effective per-subaccount caps | `subaccount_operator_settings` row, `operator_runs.settings_snapshot` (top-level column, NOT in checkpoint_payload) | `operator_runs.settings_snapshot` wins for an in-flight chain link; current `subaccount_operator_settings` wins for new dispatches |
949:| Conversation history | per-link artefacts vs `checkpoint_payload.last_action_summary` | artefacts win (the summary is an operator hint) |
950:| Fallback-stickiness state | latest non-superseded `operator_runs.credential_mode` for the task, vs broker `operator-session.usability_restored` events, vs `task.operator.credential_refreshed` audit events | derived per Â§ 3.7 item 6; no separate column. The most recent of the three signals wins; absence of clearing signals after an `'api_key'` link means stickiness persists. |
951:| Sandbox compute cost | `llm_requests` `sandbox_compute` row vs `operator_runs.cost_sandbox_compute_cents` mirror column | `llm_requests` is canonical. `operator_runs.cost_sandbox_compute_cents` is a read-cache, updated ONLY by `operatorCostWriter.writeRowsForChainLink()` in the SAME transaction that writes the ledger row. Readers that see a disagreement must trust the ledger. |
952:| Profile-volume location | `operator_runs.profile_volume_id` (cached pointer), `operator_task_profiles.volume_id` (canonical) | `operator_task_profiles.volume_id` wins; the cached pointer is invalidated if `operator_task_profiles.attempt_number > operator_runs.attempt_number` |
953:| Concurrent-session slot count | `count(*) FROM operator_runs WHERE status='running' AND ...`, the slot-allocator's in-memory cache (if any) | DB query inside an `pg_advisory_xact_lock(hashtext('operator_slots:' || subaccount_id))`-held transaction always wins; no in-memory cache is permitted in V1 |
954:

 succeeded in 718ms:
140:
141:## 3. Domain model
142:
143:### 3.1 The adapter (`operator_managed`)
144:
145:- **Id:** `operator_managed` (V1).
146:- **Forward-compat slot:** `operator_external` reserved as a type slot only â€” no registration in V1. Phase 5 adds it once BYO compute is on the roadmap.
147:- **Location:** `server/services/executionBackends/operatorManagedBackend.ts` (new file). Registered at `server/index.ts:687-691` alongside the existing five adapters.
148:- **Cost model:** `'subscription'` when the broker returns `authType: 'operator_session'`; `'per_token'` when it returns `'api_key'` fallback. The adapter does NOT inspect provider-specific credential shapes â€” those stay inside the broker. The adapter DOES branch on the broker-returned redacted `credential_mode` for three narrow purposes: credential injection (which envelope to pass to the sandbox), fallback stickiness derivation (Â§ 3.7 item 6), and cost attribution (Â§ 3.12). The `costModel` declared on the adapter object is `'subscription'`; the per-chain-link rows respect the actual `credential_mode` value.
149:- **Sandbox requirement:** `'code_execution'` (matches Spec B's primitive).
150:- **`completedEventQueue`:** `'operator-session-completed'` (pg-boss queue name).
151:- **`terminalStateTable`:** `'operator_runs'` (the table this spec introduces; mirrors `iee_runs`).
152:- **Naming discipline.** The vendor codename "OpenClaw" appears nowhere in code, schema, UI, telemetry, or customer-facing surfaces. The specific vendor product underneath is named only in vendor-specific config files (`infra/sandbox-templates/operator-session/Dockerfile`, env manifest entries). The renames listed at Â§ 5 are applied in the same change-set.
153:
154:### 3.2 Capabilities and `long_running` propagation
155:
156:The adapter declares capabilities `['delegated', 'code_execution', 'long_running', 'cancellation', 'session_identity']`.
157:
158:Both `'long_running'` AND `'session_identity'` are **new** in this spec â€” added to `ExecutionCapability` at `server/services/executionBackends/types.ts:86-93`. (`'session_identity'` was referenced by Spec C but never added to the union there; this spec adds both literals in the same edit.) Both are declared on `operator_managed`; `'long_running'` gates chain-resume behaviour, `'session_identity'` is non-gating at runtime in V1. The propagation invariant has three rules:
159:
160:1. **Single source of truth.** `'long_running'` is added to the union exactly once, in `types.ts`. All consumers import the union/type â€” they MUST NOT redeclare or restringify the literal in non-adapter / non-fixture code.
161:2. **Zero ad-hoc literals in consumers.** A new CI gate (`scripts/gates/verify-execution-capability-references.sh`) greps the repo for any naked occurrence of the literal `'long_running'` outside the canonical definition. CI fails on a naked occurrence in any of: routes, services other than adapter objects, hooks, jobs, client code. **Permitted occurrences** (enumerated in the gate's allow-list):
162:   - The canonical definition in `server/services/executionBackends/types.ts`.
163:   - Adapter object declarations under `server/services/executionBackends/*.ts` (the literal is type-checked against the `ExecutionCapability` union at the declaration site â€” drift cannot occur silently).
164:   - Test fixtures / spec strings under `__tests__/` and `*.test.ts` that consume the literal as part of asserting capability behaviour.
165:   - Documentation, this spec, the brief, this gate's own script.
166:3. **Type-checker is the enforcement for adapter declarations.** Because adapter `capabilities` arrays are typed as `ExecutionCapability[]`, mistyping `'long_running'` as `'longrunning'` is a compile error. The CI gate covers the non-adapter consumer surface (routes, services, hooks, jobs, client code) where the literal would otherwise leak.
167:
168:Spec author verifies via grep before declaring the capability-propagation chunk done; CI gate runs on every commit thereafter.
169:
170:### 3.3 `operator_runs` (chain-link rows)
171:
172:A new tenant-scoped table parallel to `iee_runs`. One row per chain link. Locked column shape:
173:
174:| Column | Type | Notes |
175:|---|---|---|
176:| `id` | `uuid PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid()` | Row id. |
177:| `agent_run_id` | `uuid NOT NULL REFERENCES agent_runs(id) ON DELETE RESTRICT` | The parent task. |
178:| `organisation_id` | `uuid NOT NULL` | RLS scope. |
179:| `subaccount_id` | `uuid NOT NULL` | RLS scope; defence-in-depth on broker subaccount-match (Â§ 3.6). |
180:| `chain_seq` | `integer NOT NULL` | Starts at 1; increments per chain link of the task. |
181:| `parent_chain_link_id` | `uuid NULL REFERENCES operator_runs(id) ON DELETE SET NULL` | NULL on chain link 1. |
182:| `attempt_number` | `integer NOT NULL DEFAULT 1` | Per Â§ 3.15 item 7 fresh-profile restart semantics. Bumps on each fresh-profile restart of the parent task. |
183:| `superseded_by_attempt` | `integer NULL` | Set to `N+1` on prior attempts of the task; the current attempt is `NULL`. |
184:| `image_tag` | `text NOT NULL` | Pinned per chain link per D4. |
185:| `vendor_session_id` | `text NULL` | Opaque vendor-side session id; surfaced in Run Trace and incidents. NULL until `dispatch()` returns it. |
186:| `credential_mode` | `text NOT NULL CHECK (credential_mode IN ('operator_session','api_key'))` | Mode for this chain link; sticky per Â§ 3.7 item 6. |
187:| `status` | `text NOT NULL CHECK (status IN ('pending','running','completed','failed','cancelled'))` | Chain-link lifecycle. |
188:| `failure_reason` | `text NULL` | Closed set; see Â§ 4.7 / Â§ 10.7. |
189:| `failed_mid_step` | `boolean NOT NULL DEFAULT false` | Sub-flag set when a `failed` chain link hit hard cap (soft + grace) without reaching a checkpoint-safe state (Â§ 3.14, D7). |
190:| `started_at` | `timestamptz NULL` | NULL until the sandbox session begins. |
191:| `completed_at` | `timestamptz NULL` | Wall-clock terminal time. |
192:| `event_emitted_at` | `timestamptz NULL` | Set non-null after the pg-boss `operator-session-completed` event is emitted (Spec A pattern). |
193:| `cost_subscription_mediated_cents` | `integer NOT NULL DEFAULT 0` | Always 0 in V1; reserved for future. |
194:| `cost_sandbox_compute_cents` | `integer NOT NULL DEFAULT 0` | Mirror of the ledger value for cheap reads; ledger is the source of truth. |
195:| `step_count` | `integer NOT NULL DEFAULT 0` | Operator turns within this chain link. |
196:| `last_progress_at` | `timestamptz NULL` | Updated on every step boundary; heartbeat-stale backstop reference. |
197:| `settings_snapshot` | `jsonb NOT NULL` | Effective `subaccount_operator_settings` values captured at dispatch time. All in-flight cap enforcement (soft cap, grace window, budget cap, max chain length, max wall-clock, concurrency cap) reads this snapshot â€” NOT the current settings row. Shape: the same six fields enumerated in Â§ 3.16. |
198:| `cancel_requested_at` | `timestamptz NULL` | Set by task-level cancellation path (Â§ 3.10 step 1). The operator runtime checks `cancel_requested_at IS NOT NULL` at each step boundary. |
199:| `cancel_requested_by_user_id` | `uuid NULL REFERENCES users(id)` | Audit: who issued the cancel. NULL until cancellation is requested. |
200:| `checkpoint_payload` | `jsonb NULL` | Encrypted-at-rest where existing infra supports it (per Â§ 3.14 item 10). NULL until a checkpoint-safe state is reached. |
201:| `profile_volume_id` | `text NULL` | Pointer (not raw filesystem path) to the persistent browser profile volume; FK semantics tracked in `operator_task_profiles` (Â§ 3.15). |
202:| `created_at` | `timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()` | Audit. |
203:| `updated_at` | `timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()` | Audit. |
204:
205:**Indexes:**
206:
207:- `(agent_run_id, attempt_number, chain_seq)` UNIQUE â€” at most one chain link per `(task, attempt, seq)`. `chain_seq` restarts at 1 for each `attempt_number` (per Â§ 3.15 item 7 fresh-profile restart semantics).
208:- `(organisation_id, subaccount_id, status)` â€” common dashboard query.
209:- `(status, last_progress_at)` partial WHERE `status = 'running'` â€” heartbeat-stale reconcile scan.
210:
211:**RLS policy:** standard org+subaccount scoping; see Â§ 6. `FORCE ROW LEVEL SECURITY` enabled to defeat owner-bypass.
212:
213:**Manifest entry** in `server/config/rlsProtectedTables.ts` added in the same implementation chunk/commit as the migration (the manifest is a TypeScript module; `policyMigration` points at the SQL migration file).
214:
215:### 3.4 `agent_runs` state-set extension
216:
217:The parent task's status enum extends to include the new task-level states. The closed set after this spec:
218:
219:```
220:'pending' | 'running' | 'delegated' |
221:'paused_for_chain_continuation' | 'paused_chain_failure' | 'paused_budget_exceeded' |
222:'completed' | 'failed' | 'cancelled'
223:```
224:
225:`'pending'`, `'running'`, `'delegated'`, `'completed'`, `'failed'`, `'cancelled'` already exist. **New** in this spec:
226:- `'paused_for_chain_continuation'` â€” scheduler-owned wait OR FIFO queue for next chain dispatch (Â§ 3.14, Â§ 3.17).
227:- `'paused_chain_failure'` â€” three consecutive dispatch failures (Â§ 3.17 item 1) OR a running chain link terminating with `failed_mid_step=true` from hard-cap unresumable (Â§ 3.14 item 3). Hard-cap unresumable counts in the same consecutive-failure budget as dispatch failures.
228:- `'paused_budget_exceeded'` â€” task paused because a time-budget guard fired. Covers both per-task budget cap (Â§ 3.17 item 4) and max wall-clock per task (Â§ 3.14 item 4); `failure_reason` distinguishes (`'budget_cap_exceeded'` vs `'max_wall_clock_exceeded'`).
229:
230:**Task-terminal states are `completed | failed | cancelled` only.** The three `paused_*` states are resumable/non-terminal â€” they emit task-state-change events (UI updates, user notifications, scheduler suspension) but DO NOT trigger terminal artefact/cost finalisation. Cost rows for chain links that completed before the pause are written normally per Â§ 3.12. The customer-visible terminal rollup is reserved for the true terminal states. Downstream consumers (cost dashboards, audit, evals) MUST NOT treat partial/pause-state rollups as final. See Â§ 10.4 for the terminal-event guarantee.
231:
232:A migration extends the existing `agent_runs.status` CHECK constraint (or text-typed allow-list, whichever the current schema uses). The migration is forward-compatible â€” existing status values are unchanged.
233:
234:The same migration adds a new column `operator_chain_failure_count integer NOT NULL DEFAULT 0` to `agent_runs`. It counts **consecutive** chain-link dispatch failures since the last successful dispatch (per Â§ 7.3 item 5). The chain-link dispatcher is the sole writer:
235:
236:- Increment under `UPDATE agent_runs SET operator_chain_failure_count = operator_chain_failure_count + 1 WHERE id = $1 AND status IN ('delegated','paused_for_chain_continuation','paused_chain_failure','paused_budget_exceeded')`. The dispatcher's queued-job reason gate (Â§ 7.3 step 2) ensures retries from paused states are only counted when the queued reason matches the current paused-state resume action.
237:- Reset to 0 on (a) a successful chain-link dispatch and (b) a user-initiated retry (the `task.operator.chain_failure_retried` audit event path).
238:
239:**State machine â€” `agent_runs` task lifecycle (operator-managed paths only):**
240:
241:```
242:pending â†’ delegated  (on first chain-link dispatch)
243:delegated â†’ paused_for_chain_continuation  (on chain-link checkpoint terminal)
244:paused_for_chain_continuation â†’ delegated  (on next chain-link dispatch)
245:delegated â†’ paused_chain_failure  (on 3rd consecutive chain-link start failure)
246:paused_chain_failure â†’ delegated  (on user-initiated retry)
247:delegated â†’ paused_budget_exceeded  (on per-task budget cap hit)
248:paused_budget_exceeded â†’ delegated  (on user budget extension)
249:delegated â†’ completed | failed  (on task-terminal event from final chain link)
250:{pending | delegated | paused_*} â†’ cancelled  (on user cancel)
251:```
252:
253:Forbidden: any transition from a terminal state. Forbidden: `pending â†’ completed` (a task MUST be delegated before terminating). The forbidden transitions are enforced by an optimistic predicate in the writer (see Â§ 10.3).
254:
255:### 3.5 Sandbox template (`operator-session`)
256:
257:- **Template path:** `infra/sandbox-templates/operator-session/`. Single source of truth for both e2b (template) and `docker-compose` (local dev).
258:- **Rename from `openclaw-session`.** The current branch already carries `infra/sandbox-templates/openclaw-session/`. This spec renames that directory to `operator-session` in the same change-set. Files renamed: `Dockerfile`, `entrypoint.sh`, `README.md`, `CURRENT_VERSION`. Image-tag references in `operator_runs.image_tag`, the CI publish job (`.github/workflows/publish-sandbox-templates.yml`), and any docker-compose service name are updated. Git history preserves the rename via `git mv`.
259:- **Image contents.** The vendor operator runtime (pinned version), the model-invocation CLI it ships with, runtime dependencies. The spec author pins the specific vendor product and version inside the Dockerfile; the codename is local to this file only.
260:- **Vendor preservation across the rename.** The V1 Dockerfile MUST preserve the existing `openclaw-session` template's vendor runtime and pinned version unchanged during the rename to `operator-session`. Any version change requires a separate spec amendment (the runtime APIs the adapter binds to and the error-classification set in `operatorRuntimeErrors.ts` are load-bearing on this version). The rename is a path-only change.
261:- **CI rebuild.** Reuses Spec B's image-build pipeline. Republishes when the Dockerfile or pinned vendor version changes.
262:- **Pinned per chain link.** `operator_runs.image_tag` records the specific image used. In-flight chain links complete on their original image when the vendor releases a new version; only new chain links get the new image. **In particular: a single task's chain links can run on different image tags** (link 1 on tag `v1.4.2`, link 17 on tag `v1.5.0` after a republish). The cost ledger and Run Trace record the image tag per chain link.
263:- **Mount points.** The persistent browser profile volume (Â§ 3.15) mounts at the browser's `user-data-dir` path on chain-link start. The Spec B sandbox isolation policy applies â€” adapter MUST assert task-subaccount matches credential-subaccount before mounting.
264:### 3.6 Credential injection (broker abstraction)
265:
266:- Adapter calls `credentialBrokerService.requestOperatorSessionCredential({ subaccountId, agentRunId })` at chain-link start.
267:- The broker returns an `OperatorSessionEnvelope` (Spec C contract) when usable, OR signals "unavailable" via the contract's existing failure mode. Raw tokens never leave the broker.
268:- **Subaccount-match assertion (defence in depth).** Before injection, the adapter asserts the returned credential's subaccount matches the `agent_runs.subaccount_id` AND `operator_runs.subaccount_id`. Mismatch is a hard fail with typed error `OPERATOR_SUBACCOUNT_MISMATCH`; chain-link status `failed`; incident emitted via `recordIncident()` with `failure_class: 'permanent'` (not a transient â€” points to a broker bug or a config drift, not a network hiccup).
269:- **What flows into the sandbox.** Only the redacted envelope's `credentialId` reference + the minimal start-time injection the operator runtime needs. The adapter MUST NOT log, persist, or print envelope contents in app logs.
270:- **What the adapter MAY consume from the envelope.** The redacted `authType` (which it maps 1:1 to `credential_mode`), the `planTier` (for cost-attribution context only), and the `usabilityState` (which is asserted to be `'connected_usable'` before injection; any other state is a hard fail with typed error `OPERATOR_SESSION_NOT_USABLE`). The adapter MUST NOT inspect `provider`-specific shapes â€” those live inside the broker.
271:
272:### 3.7 Operator-session â†’ API-key fallback
273:
274:The single biggest production-readiness item. Without it, a rate-limit or suspension mid-run is a silent failure or a hard error with no graceful path.
275:
276:1. **Failure detection â€” closed signal set.** The operator runtime + CLI surface errors classified by the adapter as `session_unavailable` when ANY of:
277:   - HTTP `401`/`403` with provider-specific bodies indicating revocation/suspension/scope-stripped (concrete patterns enumerated in `operatorRuntimeErrors.ts`).
278:   - HTTP `429` with `Retry-After` â‰¥ 60s OR the provider's "session suspended" payload.
279:   - Broker refresh failure with `expired_refresh_token | provider_revoked | insufficient_scope` (Spec C classifications).
280:   - Connection-level errors > 3 consecutive retries against the operator runtime.
281:
282:2. **Fallback resolution.** Adapter calls `credentialBrokerService.resolveFallback({ subaccountId, agentRunId, originalCredentialId })`. The broker returns `{ envelope: OperatorSessionEnvelope | ApiKeyEnvelope, mode: 'operator_session' | 'api_key' } | null`.
283:
284:   `ApiKeyEnvelope` is declared in `server/services/credentialBrokerService.ts` with shape `{ credentialId: string, connectionId: string, authType: 'api_key', provider: string, issuedAt: string, expiresAt: string | null }`. Raw API key material remains broker-internal and never leaves the broker â€” the adapter consumes the envelope reference (`credentialId`) only, mirroring the `OperatorSessionEnvelope` discipline. (Spec C reserved this seam; the spec author wires the broker side in the same chunk that wires the adapter side.)
285:
286:3. **Mid-run credential swap.** When fallback exists, the adapter:
287:   - Pauses the operator runtime via its in-band pause signal (vendor-specific; concrete API named in the implementation chunk).
288:   - Hot-swaps credentials inside the running sandbox via the same injection seam used at chain-link start.
289:   - Resumes; retries the failing turn once.
290:   - Emits `operator-session.fallback_engaged` lifecycle event (Â§ 4.7) with `chain_link_id`, `from_mode: 'operator_session'`, `to_mode: 'api_key'`, `reason: <failure-class>`, `step_index`.
291:   - Sets `operator_runs.credential_mode = 'api_key'` for the remainder of this chain link.
292:
293:4. **Hard-fail path.** If fallback resolution returns `null`, the chain link fails with typed error `OPERATOR_SESSION_UNAVAILABLE`. The chain-link row is written `status='failed', failure_reason='OPERATOR_SESSION_UNAVAILABLE'`. The customer sees the modal `r9-modal-operator-unavailable.html` pattern surfaced over the existing task surface (canonical component path chosen by the implementation chunk).
294:
295:5. **Cost-ledger semantics on mid-run swap.** The same chain link may produce **two** cost rows of the `credential_mode` boundary type: one `subscription_mediated` row for the pre-swap turns (`step_count` = turns up to swap) and one `per_token` row via the normal `llm_requests` path for the post-swap turns. Spec Â§ 3.12 enumerates the attribution rules in full.
296:
297:6. **Fallback stickiness across chain links â€” derivation rule.** Stickiness is NOT stored as a separate column. It is derived at chain-link dispatch time from existing state:
298:   - Read the latest non-superseded `operator_runs` row for the task (highest `chain_seq` where `attempt_number = current_attempt_number` AND `superseded_by_attempt IS NULL`).
299:   - Compute the row's **link-boundary timestamp** as `coalesce(event_emitted_at, completed_at, started_at)`. (`event_emitted_at` is NULL until the finaliser stamps it; `completed_at` and `started_at` are progressively earlier-set anchors that survive partial finaliser failures.)
300:   - If that row's `credential_mode = 'api_key'` AND no `operator-session.usability_restored` event has fired since the link-boundary timestamp for the same `agent_run_id` AND no `task.operator.credential_refreshed` audit event has fired since the link-boundary timestamp â†’ stickiness applies; chain link N+1 starts with `credential_mode = 'api_key'`.
301:   - Otherwise stickiness clears; chain link N+1 starts with the normal `operator_session` resolution.
302:   Both clearing signals (`operator-session.usability_restored` and `task.operator.credential_refreshed`) are looked up by querying the existing event/audit stores (already RLS-scoped to the task). Run Trace renders the `fallback_engaged` event once at the chain-link boundary where it first applied; subsequent chain links inheriting fallback show a passive `credential_mode: api_key` indicator without re-emitting the lifecycle event. The pure helper that implements the derivation lives in `operatorManagedBackendPure.ts` (Â§ 5.1) and is unit-tested per Â§ 12.
303:
304:### 3.8 Token-lifecycle handling mid-session
305:
306:- Adapter proactively triggers `credentialBrokerService.refresh({ credentialId })` at `expiresAt - REFRESH_LEAD_TIME_MS` (default 60s; configured via env, not per-subaccount).
307:- If a token expires mid-LLM-call inside the sandbox: the operator runtime surfaces a typed `auth_expired` signal; adapter triggers refresh, swaps the credential in-band, retries the failing turn once.
308:- If refresh fails with `expired_refresh_token | provider_revoked | insufficient_scope` (Spec C classifications): the broker marks the credential `revoked`; adapter routes through Â§ 3.7 fallback resolution.
309:- Refresh failures are typed lifecycle events `operator-session.refresh_failed` (Â§ 4.7) but are NOT incidents on their own â€” only the resulting chain-link-start-failure (Â§ 3.17) triggers an incident if the failure is not recovered by fallback.
310:
311:### 3.9 Mid-session progress visibility
312:
313:Two layers, mirroring the existing IEE pattern:
314:
315:- **Session-level events (push).** Operator runtime step boundaries surface to the adapter; the adapter:
316:  1. Enqueues a `'operator-session-progressed'` pg-boss event payload `{ runId, chainLinkId, stepIndex, summary, timestamp }` with idempotency key `(operator_run_id, step_index)` (per Â§ 10.1). The adapter does NOT mutate `operator_runs.last_progress_at` or `step_count` directly.
317:  2. The pg-boss handler (`operatorSessionProgressedHandler.ts`) is the SOLE writer for `last_progress_at` and `step_count` (see Â§ 7.4 for the exact SQL with NULL-safety and the `status='running'` post-terminal guard).
318:  3. The handler then bridges to the WebSocket `agent-run:{runId}` room via `emitAgentRunUpdate(runId, 'operator-session.progressed', payload)`.
319:
320:- **Polling fallback (pull).** `GET /api/operator-sessions/:operatorRunId/progress` returns the latest progress snapshot from the `operator_runs` row. Route mirrors `server/routes/iee.ts:GET /api/iee/runs/:ieeRunId/progress`. Same auth gates: `authenticate`, `requirePermission('AGENT_RUN_READ')`, subaccount scoping via `getOrgScopedDb()`.
321:
322:The polling route exists because (a) the WebSocket bridge can be down without the run being broken, and (b) some agent-run consumers don't keep a socket open. The brief is explicit that V1 keeps polling as the visibility primitive; streaming progress is deferred to Phase 3.5.
323:
324:### 3.10 Cancellation (chain-aware)
325:
326:The adapter declares `'cancellation'` capability. Spec A's contract gives one method: `cancel({ runId, backendTaskId })`. The Operator Backend's implementation order at the **chain-link level**:
327:
328:1. **Operator runtime native hook.** If the runtime exposes a cancel endpoint (vendor-specific), the adapter calls it first.
329:2. **Per-step-boundary check.** Adapter sets `operator_runs.cancel_requested_at = now()` and `cancel_requested_by_user_id = $actor` (Â§ 3.3); the operator runtime polls these fields at each step boundary and exits cleanly when `cancel_requested_at IS NOT NULL`.
330:3. **Heartbeat-stale backstop.** Spec A's shared reconcile loop catches chain links stuck in `running` with `last_progress_at` older than `HEARTBEAT_STALE_MS` (default 5 minutes) and marks them `failed` with `failure_reason='heartbeat_stale'`.
331:
332:**Task-level cancellation semantics** are chain-aware. When a user cancels a task:
333:
334:1. **Cancel the active chain link** â€” writes `operator_runs.status = 'cancelled'` (only if currently `'pending' | 'running'`; otherwise no-op).
335:2. **Drain queued chain-continuation jobs** â€” remove FIFO-queued continuation entries (Â§ 3.17 item 5) for this task from the scheduler queue. Atomic with step 3.
336:3. **Prevent further chain dispatch** â€” set `agent_runs.status = 'cancelled'` via the optimistic predicate `UPDATE agent_runs SET status='cancelled' WHERE id = $1 AND status IN ('delegated','paused_for_chain_continuation','paused_chain_failure','paused_budget_exceeded','pending')`. 0 rows-affected means the task is already in a terminal state; return `409` with the current state.
337:4. **Emit the task-terminal event** â€” `operator-session.task_cancelled` (Â§ 4.7). The finaliser performs full rollup.
338:5. **Schedule profile retention/GC** â€” set `operator_task_profiles.scheduled_gc_at = now() + INTERVAL '48 hours'` per Â§ 3.15 item 4 (default retention).
339:
340:Cancellation from a paused state follows the same task-level path: drain scheduler state, mark `agent_runs.status='cancelled'`, fire task-terminal event, schedule profile GC.
341:
342:**Concurrency guard.** Steps 1, 2, 3 happen inside one `withOrgTx`-scoped transaction. If two concurrent cancels race, the first writes `status='cancelled'`; the second sees 0 rows-affected on step 3 and returns `409` to the losing caller. No double-emit of the terminal event.
343:### 3.11 Run Trace integration
344:
345:The adapter MUST emit Run Trace events for: session start, credential injected (auth-type redacted), each step boundary, fallback engaged (if any), chain-link terminal status, artefact harvest, task-terminal status (final chain link only).
346:
347:Reuses the virtual-view Run Trace contract from the SynthetOS foundation refactor. New event-type families:
348:
349:- `operator-session.*` (lifecycle): see Â§ 4.7.
350:- `operator.*` (incidents, audit, system): see Â§ 4.8, Â§ 4.9.
351:
352:**Chain-link merged view.** Run Trace renders the chain as a single merged timeline with `chain link N starts` dividers (per mockup `r17-runtrace-chain-link-divider.html`). The renderer changes are scoped to `client/src/pages/operate/components/RunTraceEventRenderer.tsx` â€” a new `<ChainLinkDivider>` element inserts between events belonging to different `chain_seq` values.
353:
354:**Attempt grouping.** When a task has `attempt_number > 1` (fresh-profile restart per Â§ 3.15 item 7), Run Trace renders attempts as **top-level groups** above the chain-link structure. Superseded attempts are collapsed by default; the current attempt is the default-expanded view. The merged-timeline view above spans only the current attempt; cross-attempt comparison is a separate (future) view.
355:
356:**Sensitive content.** Checkpoint payloads (page URLs, screenshots) are NOT rendered in Run Trace by default â€” they live in `operator_runs.checkpoint_payload` and surface only through the harvested-artefact path (Â§ 3.12) when promoted. See Â§ 3.14 item 10 for the full policy.
357:
358:### 3.12 Per-customer cost visibility
359:
360:Even when LLM cost is zero (subscription-prepaid), sandbox compute is real spend. The adapter writes to the cost ledger:
361:
362:**A. Sandbox compute (real spend, every chain link).**
363:
364:One `source_type: 'sandbox_compute'` row per chain link / sandbox session. Inputs taken from Spec B's `SandboxRunTaskOutput`: `vCPUSeconds`, `wallClockMs`, `peakMemoryBytes`. Cost is computed by the existing sandbox-compute pricing function (Spec B). The ledger row carries the chain link's `operator_run_id` and is joined to the parent task at read time via `agent_run_id`.
365:
366:**B. Subscription-mediated (zero-cost accounting, per chain link).**
367:
368:One `source_type: 'subscription_mediated'` row per chain link where the chain link **started under** `credential_mode = 'operator_session'` (even if a mid-run fallback later switched the row's final `credential_mode` to `'api_key'`). The cost-writer derives eligibility from: (a) the chain link's START mode (preserved via the row's `started_at` snapshot semantics â€” see below), OR equivalently (b) the presence of a `fallback_engaged` event with `from_mode='operator_session'` for this chain link. The final `operator_runs.credential_mode` value is NOT the trigger.
369:
370:Implementation note: the writer queries the lifecycle event store for `operator-session.fallback_engaged` for this `operator_run_id`; presence of such an event means the chain link DID start with `operator_session` regardless of the final column value, and `subscription_mediated` writes the pre-swap portion (`step_count` = `fallback_engaged.step_index`, by the cost-writer pure helper).
371:
372:Row carries:
373:
374:| Field | Value |
375:|---|---|
376:| `source_type` | `'subscription_mediated'` |
377:| `cost_cents` | `0` |
378:| `agent_run_id` | parent task |
379:| `operator_run_id` | chain-link id |
380:| `chain_seq` | chain-link sequence number |
381:| `vendor_session_id` | the opaque vendor session id (audit) |
382:| `credential_mode` | `'operator_session'` |
383:| `step_count` | turns within this chain link |
384:| `plan_tier` | from the broker envelope (audit context) |
385:
386:**C. Per-token (mid-run swap or fully-fallback chain link).**
387:
388:When fallback engages mid-chain-link: turns BEFORE the swap â†’ counted in the chain link's `subscription_mediated` row (with `step_count` reflecting only the pre-swap turns); turns AFTER the swap â†’ flow through the normal `llm_requests` writer with `source_type: 'per_token'`. The boundary is recorded in the `operator-session.fallback_engaged` event payload.
389:
390:When a full chain link runs under fallback (`credential_mode = 'api_key'` from chain-link start): NO `subscription_mediated` row is written; only `per_token` rows via `llm_requests`. The `sandbox_compute` row is still written.
391:
392:**Aggregation:** dashboards use the existing usage views. The `(agent_run_id, source_type)` index on `llm_requests` (or equivalent) supports the rollup. **No new dashboard is built in V1** â€” data must be queryable from existing usage views.
393:
394:**Idempotency posture (per Â§ 10.1):**
395:
396:- The `subscription_mediated` and `sandbox_compute` chain-link-summary writers are **key-based idempotent** on `(operator_run_id, source_type, boundary)`. Boundary key for `subscription_mediated` is `(operator_run_id, 'subscription_mediated', 'chain_link')`; for `sandbox_compute`: `(operator_run_id, 'sandbox_compute', 'chain_link')`. Many turns may occur within a chain link, but the cost writer emits exactly ONE summary row per `(operator_run_id, source_type)`.
397:- `per_token` rows (one per LLM call, potentially many per chain link) retain the existing `(agent_run_id, request_id)` idempotency from the LLM-request writer. The new `operator_run_id` column on `llm_requests` is nullable attribution only â€” it does NOT participate in the per-token row's idempotency key.
398:
399:A retry after partial commit MUST NOT double-write. The chain-link summary writers are invoked exactly once per chain-link terminal event via the finaliser hook (Spec A pattern), not from the adapter's hot path.
400:
401:**Concurrency guard (per Â§ 10.3):** the cost-writer holds an advisory lock on `(operator_run_id)` for the duration of the rollup transaction. Two concurrent finalises (rare; only possible if the pg-boss event handler retries before idempotency catches it) cannot interleave row writes.
402:
403:### 3.13 CS runbook for provider account suspension
404:
405:Per Spec C Decision 3 risk #1: the customer will blame SynthetOS regardless of what they signed at opt-in. Before the first Plus-tier opt-in customer hits a suspension:
406:
407:- **Runbook.** `docs/runbooks/operator-session-account-suspension.md`. Authored in this spec change-set. Sections:
408:  1. What "operator-session suspended" means (one paragraph, plain English).
409:  2. How the system detects suspension (the Â§3.7 closed signal set).
410:  3. The automatic notification chain (incident â†’ CS notification â†’ assigned user inbox + admin notification).
411:  4. How to retrieve the disclosure record by `consent_record_id` (Spec C).
412:  5. Comms templates (apology, fact-based, with disclosure link).
413:  6. Customer's options (reconnect, add fallback API key, cancel ongoing tasks).
414:  7. Escalation tree.
415:
416:- **Comms templates.** `docs/runbooks/templates/operator-session-suspension-customer-email.md`, `.../in-app-message.md`. Plain English; refers to the disclosure record without legal jargon.
417:
418:- **Automatic detection.** The Â§3.7 fallback path emits a typed `system-monitor` notification on the first `OPERATOR_SESSION_UNAVAILABLE` hit AND on `usability_state` flipping from `'connected_usable'` to anything else (broker-side change). The CS notification is the typed event `cs.operator_session.suspended_detected` produced by `notifyOperatorSessionSuspended()` (`server/services/operatorSessionSuspensionNotifier.ts`, Â§ 5.1) and consumed by the existing inbox pipeline â€” no new pipeline component is introduced.
419:
420:Small artefact (one-pager + comms templates + the typed CS notification wiring) but it blocks first Plus-tier onboarding. Belongs in this change-set, not deferred â€” the moment the adapter ships to a Plus-tier customer, the runbook is on the critical path.

 succeeded in 748ms:
421:### 3.14 Chain-resume model
422:
423:A single operator task spans many 120-min chain-link sessions. Each session is a "chain link." When the soft cap approaches, the operator drives itself to a checkpoint, persists state, and the session ends. A scheduler picks up the task and dispatches the next chain link, which resumes from the checkpoint. The user sees one task progressing, not many separate runs.
424:
425:1. **Chain-link data model.** Locked in Â§ 3.3. `chain_seq` starts at 1; `parent_chain_link_id` FKs to the prior chain link; `checkpoint_payload` JSONB holds (or points to) the resume state.
426:
427:2. **Checkpoint contents (minimum).** Â§ 4.6 pins the JSONB shape. Required fields: `original_task_brief_ref`, `conversation_history_pointer` (artefact-store reference, not inline blob), `current_page_url`, `last_action_summary`, `next_planned_step`, `last_state_screenshot_artefact_id` (pointer; the screenshot lives in the artefact store).
428:
429:3. **Soft cap + auto-extend.**
430:   - Soft cap = `subaccount_operator_settings.session_soft_cap_minutes` (default 120, range 30â€“240, per Â§ 3.16).
431:   - At `T - 10 min`, the operator emits a `'preparing_checkpoint'` step-state signal. The adapter enqueues an `operator-session-progressed` event with the step-state `preparing_checkpoint`; per Â§ 3.9 / Â§ 7.4, `operatorSessionProgressedHandler.ts` is the sole writer for `last_progress_at` and `step_count`. The handler bridges the state to the WebSocket room.
432:   - **`is_resumable_now` emission contract.** The operator runtime MUST emit `is_resumable_now` as a boolean field in the checkpoint step-state payload consumed by `operatorManagedBackend.dispatch()` (the payload shape is the same step-state envelope used for progress events; the build chunk pins the exact vendor field). Absent or malformed values are treated as `false` and the chain link is logged with `failure_reason='checkpoint_signal_invalid'`.
433:   - If at the soft cap the operator's `is_resumable_now` boolean is `true`, the chain link terminates `'completed'` with `checkpoint_payload` non-null.
434:   - If `is_resumable_now` is `false` at the soft cap, the adapter auto-extends up to `subaccount_operator_settings.auto_extend_grace_minutes` (default 30, range 0â€“60, per Â§ 3.16).
435:   - At soft-cap + grace, the chain link terminates `'failed'` with `failure_reason='hard_cap_unresumable'` and `failed_mid_step=true`. The task transitions IMMEDIATELY to `paused_chain_failure` â€” this is a single-event pause, NOT a 3-failure threshold. The "three consecutive failures" threshold in Â§ 3.17 item 1 applies only to chain-link START failures (`pending`-state failures). Hard-cap unresumable increments `operator_chain_failure_count` for diagnostic visibility only; it does NOT need three occurrences to trigger the pause. Recovery (user-initiated retry from `paused_chain_failure`) resets the counter.
436:
437:4. **Chain-link dispatch.** End of chain link N writes `checkpoint_payload` and emits `'operator-session-completed'` (the standard adapter terminal event, with status `'completed'` and a non-null `checkpoint_payload` field â€” distinct from the task-terminal `'completed'`). The finaliser handler distinguishes (branches evaluated in order; first match wins):
438:   - `completed` with non-null `checkpoint_payload` AND consumed-budget-minutes â‰¥ pinned `settings_snapshot.per_task_budget_cap_minutes` â†’ task transitions to `'paused_budget_exceeded'`; do NOT enqueue the next chain link.
439:   - `completed` with non-null `checkpoint_payload` AND (`now() - first_operator_run.started_at`) â‰¥ pinned `settings_snapshot.max_wall_clock_per_task_days` â†’ task transitions to `'paused_budget_exceeded'` with `failure_reason='max_wall_clock_exceeded'`; do NOT enqueue the next chain link.
440:   - `completed` with non-null `checkpoint_payload` AND the parent task is at max chain length (`chain_seq >= settings_snapshot.max_chain_length`) â†’ task-terminal `'failed'` with `failure_reason='max_chain_length_reached'` (rolls up to `agent_runs.status='failed'`).
441:   - `completed` with non-null `checkpoint_payload` (none of the above caps tripped) â†’ dispatch next chain link via the `'operator-session-dispatch-next-chain-link'` queue.
442:   - `completed` with NULL `checkpoint_payload` AND `is_resumable_now=true` on the last step AND task scope reports "done" â†’ task-terminal `'completed'`. (The operator runtime emits a `'task_completed'` step-state when the task is genuinely done; that signal sets the writer to NULL checkpoint and triggers task termination.)
443:   - `failed` with `failed_mid_step=true` â†’ task transitions to `paused_chain_failure`; user must retry or cancel.
444:   - `failed` with `failed_mid_step=false` â†’ propagate task-terminal `'failed'` (operator runtime hard error, e.g. crash).
445:   - `cancelled` â†’ propagate task-terminal `'cancelled'`.
446:
447:5. **Resume payload.** Chain link N+1 starts with: the original task brief, the accumulated conversation-history pointer, the checkpoint from chain link N, and the persistent browser profile (Â§ 3.15) mounted. The operator's first action is to verify it's on the expected page and continue from the `next_planned_step`.
448:
449:6. **Conversation history accumulation.** Per-chain-link blobs joined at read time, capped at last N chain links of context for the operator-model invocation. Concretely: each chain link writes a single artefact `operator-conversation-link-{operator_run_id}.json` to the existing artefact store. The artefact's MIME type is `application/vnd.synthetos.operator-conversation-link+json;version=1` and its shape is the Zod schema `OperatorConversationLinkArtefact` declared in `shared/types/operatorConversationArtefact.ts` (a new file, Â§ 5.1). The resume payload composer reads the latest K (default 5) artefacts and concatenates them in chain order. K is a constant in `operatorConversationHistoryPure.ts`; not configurable per-subaccount in V1.
450:
451:7. **Terminal states + failure classification (runtime vs start vs hard-cap).**
452:   - **Runtime failure (hard error)** â€” chain link is in state `'running'` at the time of failure due to an operator-runtime crash, heartbeat-stale, or unrecoverable error that does NOT match the hard-cap-unresumable signal â†’ terminates the **task** with the chain link's failure reason (`agent_runs.status='failed'`). Remaining chain dispatch does NOT happen.
453:   - **Hard-cap unresumable** (a specific running-state failure where soft-cap + grace elapsed without a checkpoint-safe state) is routed per Â§ 3.14 item 3: chain link `'failed'` + `failed_mid_step=true`, task `paused_chain_failure`. It is NOT a hard runtime failure for the purposes of this classification.
454:   - **Start failure** â€” chain link is in state `'pending'` at the time of failure (dispatch-time, before the chain link has begun running) â†’ Â§ 3.17 retry/pause semantics apply (backoff retry then `paused_chain_failure`), NOT immediate task termination.
455:   - The state-machine boundary is at `pending â†’ running`. The transition timestamp is `operator_runs.started_at` (set by the adapter immediately after the sandbox session is created and the credential is injected).
456:
457:8. **Run Trace.** Merged timeline with `chain link N starts` dividers (Â§ 3.11). The virtual-view contract spans chain links via the `agent_run_id` join.
458:
459:9. **TaskHeader status.** Mockup `r14-taskheader-chain-link-status.html`. Three variants:
460:   - Known estimate (after first handoff): `"link N of ~M, T hrs elapsed"`. `~M` is computed as `min(max_chain_length, max(N+2, ceil(estimated_total_steps / avg_steps_per_link)))` and refreshes per chain link.
461:   - Unknown estimate (before first handoff): `"link N of â€”"`. Tooltip explains "estimate available after the first chain handoff completes."
462:   - Terminal: `"{N} sessions, {H}h {M}m total"`.
463:
464:10. **Checkpoint-payload security.** Checkpoint payloads are sensitive task artefacts and MUST be:
465:    - **Encrypted at rest** where existing artefact infrastructure supports it. Concretely: the JSONB column is written via the existing app-level encryption helper (the same helper used by `agent_run_payloads`'s redaction pipeline). The tentative file is `server/services/agentRunPayloadEncryptionService.ts` exporting `encryptAgentRunPayloadJson(value): Promise<EncryptedJson>` and `decryptAgentRunPayloadJson(value): Promise<unknown>`. If the in-tree names differ, Chunk 1 (or the chunk that first touches the checkpoint writer) MUST update this spec before implementation.
466:    - **Scoped by org/subaccount/task.** The RLS policy on `operator_runs` enforces org+subaccount; the `task_id` (= `agent_run_id`) is implicit via the FK.
467:    - **Excluded from broad logs.** The adapter MUST NOT log `checkpoint_payload` contents at any log level. A grep gate (`scripts/gates/verify-no-checkpoint-logging.sh`) bans naive log calls referencing the column.
468:    - **Redacted in Run Trace by default.** The embedded screenshot is treated as an INTERNAL recovery artefact, not customer-visible. Customer-facing screenshots flow only through the harvested-artefact path (Â§ 3.12 / artefact harvester).
469:
470:### 3.15 Persistent browser profile per task
471:
472:Smooth chain handoff requires browser state (cookies, login session, local storage) to survive across chain links. Without this, every chain link starts cold, must replay credentials, and breaks on MFA.
473:
474:1. **Profile storage â€” new table `operator_task_profiles`.**
475:
476:| Column | Type | Notes |
477:|---|---|---|
478:| `id` | `uuid PRIMARY KEY DEFAULT gen_random_uuid()` | |
479:| `task_id` | `uuid NOT NULL REFERENCES agent_runs(id) ON DELETE RESTRICT` | One profile per task. |
480:| `organisation_id` | `uuid NOT NULL` | RLS scope. |
481:| `subaccount_id` | `uuid NOT NULL` | RLS scope. |
482:| `attempt_number` | `integer NOT NULL DEFAULT 1` | Bumps on fresh-profile restart (Â§ 3.15 item 7). |
483:| `volume_id` | `text NOT NULL` | Sandbox-volume id (opaque pointer; safe to log). |
484:| `size_bytes` | `bigint NOT NULL DEFAULT 0` | Updated on each chain link end. |
485:| `size_cap_bytes` | `bigint NOT NULL DEFAULT 524288000` | 500 MB default per Â§ 3.15 item 3. |
486:| `status` | `text NOT NULL CHECK (status IN ('active','scheduled_gc','gc_in_progress','gc_done'))` | Lifecycle. |
487:| `scheduled_gc_at` | `timestamptz NULL` | Set to `task_terminal_at + retention_window`. |
488:| `gc_started_at` | `timestamptz NULL` | Set on transition to `'gc_in_progress'`; cleared on transition to `'gc_done'`. The GC handler reclaims stale `'gc_in_progress'` rows (`gc_started_at < now() - INTERVAL '30 minutes'`) per Â§ 7.5. |
489:| `debug_retention_extended_by` | `uuid NULL REFERENCES users(id)` | Set when admin extends retention to 14 days. |
490:| `debug_retention_extended_at` | `timestamptz NULL` | Audit. |
491:| `created_at` | `timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()` | |
492:| `updated_at` | `timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()` | |
493:
494:Unique constraint: `(task_id, attempt_number)`.
495:
496:2. **Profile mount.** The `operator-session` Docker template mounts the volume at the browser's `user-data-dir` path on chain-link start. Mount instruction is part of the template's `entrypoint.sh`.
497:
498:3. **Profile size cap.** Default 500 MB per task. Enforced by:
499:   - Disk-usage check before chain-link start (adapter reads `size_bytes`; if `size_bytes >= size_cap_bytes`, chain link fails with `failure_reason='profile_size_cap_exceeded'`).
500:   - Docker volume quota (template-level, set in entrypoint).
501:   Cap is a system constant, NOT per-subaccount in V1.
502:
503:4. **Profile lifecycle + retention.** Volume is created on first chain-link start (`status='active'`). Persists across chain links. After task-terminal: `status='scheduled_gc', scheduled_gc_at = now() + INTERVAL '48 hours'` (default). An admin (`org_admin`) may set `debug_retention_extended_by/_at` at task-terminal time, which extends `scheduled_gc_at` to `now() + INTERVAL '14 days'` for that task. Customer-visible artefacts (per Â§ 3.12) are harvested into the artefact store BEFORE the volume is GC'd, regardless of retention window. A pg-boss cron job (`operator-task-profile-gc`, every 15 minutes) marks profiles `status='gc_in_progress'` when `now() >= scheduled_gc_at`, performs the volume delete via the sandbox provider, then sets `status='gc_done'`. Hard max lifetime including retention = `max_wall_clock_per_task_days` + 14 days.
504:
505:5. **Profile permissions.** Volume access scoped to chain links of the owning task by Spec B's sandbox isolation primitive. The adapter MUST assert `task.subaccount_id == credential.subaccount_id == profile.subaccount_id` before mounting (defence in depth, three-way check). Mismatch â†’ hard fail with typed error `OPERATOR_PROFILE_SUBACCOUNT_MISMATCH`.
506:
507:6. **First-chain-link cold start.** First chain link gets a fresh `user-data-dir`. Login from the credential broker happens naturally in the model loop â€” no special bootstrap.
508:
509:7. **Failure recovery + fresh-profile restart.** If the profile volume is corrupted or unrecoverable, chain-link start fails with typed error `OPERATOR_PROFILE_UNRECOVERABLE` and Â§ 3.17 incident path engages. Authorised users (`org_admin`) may opt to "restart task with fresh profile" â€” a per-task action with the following LOCKED semantics:
510:   - **Same `agent_run_id`** (the customer-visible identity is preserved).
511:   - **New `attempt_number`** on every `operator_runs` row from this point (and a new `operator_task_profiles` row with the bumped attempt). Default starts at `1`; bumps on each fresh-profile restart.
512:   - **Conversation history resets at the attempt boundary.** Chain link 1 of attempt N+1 starts with the ORIGINAL task brief only.
513:   - **Old chain links retained but marked `superseded_by_attempt = N+1`.** Visible in Run Trace under a collapsed "Attempt 1" group; current attempt is the default-expanded view.
514:   - **Old profile retained per Â§ 3.15 item 4 retention rules** (default 48 hr after the attempt-superseded event; admin debug-retention extends to 14 days). The new attempt's volume is created fresh.
515:   - **Audit event** `task.operator.fresh_profile_restart` (Â§ 4.9) writes `actor_user_id`, `prior_attempt_number`, `new_attempt_number`, `prior_chain_seq_count`, `request_id`.
516:   - Run Trace renders attempts as top-level groups; chain links nest under their attempt.

518:### 3.16 Per-subaccount operator settings
519:
520:Runtime limits live on the subaccount, not on the org. Subaccounts are where agents run. A new "Operator" tab on `client/src/pages/AdminSubaccountDetailPage.tsx`, inserted between Board Config (`'board'`) and Usage & Costs (`'usage'`) in the `ActiveTab` union and `TAB_LABELS` map.
521:
522:**Tab visibility:** `org_admin` can edit; `manager` can view; below `manager` cannot see the tab.
523:
524:**Fields and defaults** (locked):
525:
526:| Field | DB column | Default | Min | Max | UI section |
527:|---|---|---|---|---|---|
528:| Soft session cap (min) | `session_soft_cap_minutes` | 120 | 30 | 240 | Session limits |
529:| Auto-extend grace (min) | `auto_extend_grace_minutes` | 30 | 0 | 60 | Session limits |
530:| Max chain length | `max_chain_length` | 50 | 1 | 500 | Task limits |
531:| Max wall-clock per task (days) | `max_wall_clock_per_task_days` | 30 | 1 | 365 | Task limits |
532:| Per-task budget cap (op-session minutes) | `per_task_budget_cap_minutes` | 6000 | 60 | 60000 | Task limits |
533:| Concurrent operator sessions (per subaccount) | `concurrent_operator_sessions_cap` | 5 | 1 | 25 | Session limits |
534:
535:**Enforcement points and read sources.** Most caps are enforced from `operator_runs.settings_snapshot` for in-flight chain links and from the live `subaccount_operator_settings` row for new dispatches. The concurrency cap is a special case (both sides need the live value):
536:
537:- `session_soft_cap_minutes`, `auto_extend_grace_minutes` â€” adapter-side, per Â§ 3.14 item 3. Read from `operator_runs.settings_snapshot`.
538:- `max_chain_length` â€” finaliser decision table, per Â§ 3.14 item 4 (`chain_seq >= cap` branch). Read from `operator_runs.settings_snapshot`.
539:- `max_wall_clock_per_task_days` â€” finaliser decision table, per Â§ 3.14 item 4 (`now() - first_operator_run.started_at >= cap` â†’ `paused_budget_exceeded` with `failure_reason='max_wall_clock_exceeded'`). Read from `operator_runs.settings_snapshot`.
540:- `per_task_budget_cap_minutes` â€” finaliser decision table, per Â§ 3.14 item 4 (consumed budget branch) and Â§ 3.17 item 4. Read from `operator_runs.settings_snapshot`.
541:- `concurrent_operator_sessions_cap` â€” adapter `dispatch()`, per Â§ 3.17 item 5 (advisory-lock pattern). Read from **live** `subaccount_operator_settings` at every dispatch (both new tasks and chain continuations). The settings_snapshot's copy is for audit / incident-payload context only â€” it is NOT the enforcement source. Rationale: the concurrency cap is a subaccount-wide global, not a per-task contract; changes need to take effect immediately for new dispatches even when other in-flight tasks are using stale per-task caps.
542:
543:**Storage choice.** A new tenant-scoped table `subaccount_operator_settings` (one row per subaccount; primary key `subaccount_id`). This is preferred over adding six columns to the existing `subaccounts` table â€” keeps the operator concern isolated, and is the same shape `subaccount_optimiser_settings` already uses for the Sub-account Optimiser feature.
544:
545:| Column | Type | Notes |
546:|---|---|---|
547:| `subaccount_id` | `uuid PRIMARY KEY REFERENCES subaccounts(id) ON DELETE CASCADE` | |
548:| `organisation_id` | `uuid NOT NULL` | RLS scope (defence in depth). |
549:| `session_soft_cap_minutes` | `integer NOT NULL DEFAULT 120 CHECK (session_soft_cap_minutes BETWEEN 30 AND 240)` | |
550:| `auto_extend_grace_minutes` | `integer NOT NULL DEFAULT 30 CHECK (auto_extend_grace_minutes BETWEEN 0 AND 60)` | |
551:| `max_chain_length` | `integer NOT NULL DEFAULT 50 CHECK (max_chain_length BETWEEN 1 AND 500)` | |
552:| `max_wall_clock_per_task_days` | `integer NOT NULL DEFAULT 30 CHECK (max_wall_clock_per_task_days BETWEEN 1 AND 365)` | |
553:| `per_task_budget_cap_minutes` | `integer NOT NULL DEFAULT 6000 CHECK (per_task_budget_cap_minutes BETWEEN 60 AND 60000)` | |
554:| `concurrent_operator_sessions_cap` | `integer NOT NULL DEFAULT 5 CHECK (concurrent_operator_sessions_cap BETWEEN 1 AND 25)` | |
555:| `updated_at` | `timestamptz NOT NULL DEFAULT now()` | ETag source. |
556:| `updated_by_user_id` | `uuid NULL REFERENCES users(id)` | Audit. |
557:
558:**Defaulting.** When a chain link reads its caps and no row exists for the subaccount, the read uses the column defaults. The first write inserts the row (UPSERT pattern). No backfill migration is needed; the row is created lazily.
559:
560:**Optimistic concurrency.** Writes use `If-Match` against `updated_at` rounded to seconds (consistent with the JWT `iat` precision discipline from KNOWLEDGE.md). Mismatch returns `409 OPERATOR_SETTINGS_CONFLICT` with the current row body; UI MUST refetch and redisplay before retry.
561:
562:**Server-side validation.** Each PATCH validates against the column CHECK constraints AND the explicit min/max in the table above (defence-in-depth â€” a future CHECK loosening cannot silently widen the API).
563:
564:**Audit event.** Every successful update writes `subaccount.operator_settings.updated` (Â§ 4.9) with `before`, `after`, `actor_user_id`, `request_id`, `source` (`ui` | `api` | `system`).
565:
566:**Settings application.** Changes apply to **new chain links only** for per-task caps. An in-flight chain link uses the per-task cap that was in effect when it dispatched. The snapshot is pinned in `operator_runs.settings_snapshot` (Â§ 3.3) at dispatch time and is the sole source of truth for in-flight per-task cap enforcement (`session_soft_cap_minutes`, `auto_extend_grace_minutes`, `max_chain_length`, `max_wall_clock_per_task_days`, `per_task_budget_cap_minutes`). The `concurrent_operator_sessions_cap` is a subaccount-wide global, NOT a per-task contract â€” it is snapshotted for audit context only and is always enforced from the live `subaccount_operator_settings` row at every dispatch (both new tasks and chain continuations). The incident payload's `settings_snapshot` field (Â§ 3.17 item 2) is copied verbatim from this row. The UI surfaces a footer note: "Changes apply to new sessions only."
567:
568:### 3.17 Chain-link start failure + incident emission
569:
570:A chain link can fail to dispatch for several reasons (auth lost, runtime unavailable, profile corrupted, subaccount over concurrency cap, budget cap hit).
571:
572:1. **Backoff retry on transient failure.** Chain-link dispatch is retried with exponential backoff: 1 min, 5 min, 15 min. After **3 consecutive failures** (`agent_runs.operator_chain_failure_count >= 3`), the task transitions to `paused_chain_failure`.
573:
574:   The retry counter (`agent_runs.operator_chain_failure_count`, per Â§ 3.4) resets on:
575:   - A user-initiated retry (via the per-task "Retry" action).
576:   - A successful chain-link dispatch (i.e. counter is "consecutive failures since last successful dispatch", not lifetime).
577:
578:2. **Incident emission.** Each retry attempt writes its own incident via `recordIncident()` (`server/services/incidentIngestor.ts`). Typed event: `operator.chain_link_start_failed`. Idempotency key: `operator.chain_link_start_failed:${agent_run_id}:${attempt_number}:${chain_seq}:${retry_attempt}`. Pg-boss redelivery of the same retry attempt is a no-op. Payload (locked shape â€” Â§ 4.8):
579:
580:   ```json
581:   {
582:     "event": "operator.chain_link_start_failed",
583:     "organisation_id": "<uuid>",
584:     "subaccount_id": "<uuid>",
585:     "agent_run_id": "<uuid>",
586:     "operator_run_id": "<uuid|null>",
587:     "chain_seq": 7,
588:     "attempt_number": 1,
589:     "failure_class": "transient|permanent|budget|concurrency|profile_corruption|auth",
590:     "failure_reason": "<verbatim error string>",
591:     "request_id": "<correlation id>",
592:     "credential_mode": "operator_session|api_key|unknown",
593:     "profile_volume_id": "<opaque pointer or null>",
594:     "settings_snapshot": {
595:       "session_soft_cap_minutes": 120,
596:       "auto_extend_grace_minutes": 30,
597:       "max_chain_length": 50,
598:       "max_wall_clock_per_task_days": 30,
599:       "per_task_budget_cap_minutes": 6000,
600:       "concurrent_operator_sessions_cap": 5
601:     },
602:     "retry_attempt": 2,
603:     "is_terminal": false
604:   }
605:   ```
606:
607:   `is_terminal=true` is set on the 3rd consecutive failure that triggers `paused_chain_failure`. The system-monitoring agent owns: classifying repeated patterns across tasks (e.g. "all chain links failing on subaccount X with the same auth error" â†’ suggest re-auth flow), flagging remedies, escalating to the assigned user or org admin when an automated remedy is not available.
608:
609:3. **User notification.** On `paused_chain_failure` transition, notify the assigned user via the existing inbox/notification path. Notification payload includes the failure class and the suggested action (Retry / Cancel). User actions:
610:   - **Retry** â€” resets retry counter, dispatches next chain link from the current checkpoint (no fresh profile). Audit event `task.operator.chain_failure_retried`.
611:   - **Cancel** â€” Â§ 3.10 cancellation path.
612:
613:4. **Budget-cap auto-pause and accounting.** Hitting the per-task budget cap is NOT a failure â€” it is a deliberate auto-pause. Task transitions to `paused_budget_exceeded`.
614:
615:   **Accounting rules:**
616:   - Minutes consumed are measured using **DB-anchored timestamps** (`operator_runs.started_at` / `operator_runs.completed_at` written from `now()` inside the chain-link transaction by the adapter). NOT app-process wall-clock.
617:   - Consumption is the **actual sandbox wall-clock minutes** elapsed, not the allocated cap. A 90-minute chain link consumes 90 minutes.
618:   - When consumption hits the per-task budget cap mid-chain-link, the running chain link MUST checkpoint and pause at the **next resumable boundary** (NOT hard-kill), UNLESS the chain link also breaches the hard safety limit (soft cap + grace), in which case it terminates per Â§ 3.14 item 3 hard-cap behaviour.
619:   - Budget extension actions are additive (`new_cap = old_cap + extension_minutes`), never absolute resets, and write audit event `task.operator.budget_extended` (Â§ 4.9) with `actor_user_id`, `extension_minutes`, `request_id`, `source`.
620:   - The user can extend at increments of 60 minutes (UI offers presets +1000, +3000, plus a custom-amount input bounded 60..60000 with 60-min step per mockup `r16-modal-budget-exceeded-autopause.html`).
621:
622:5. **Concurrency-cap behaviour â€” distinguish new-task vs chain-continuation.**
623:
624:   The `concurrent_operator_sessions_cap` per subaccount is computed at dispatch time as `count of operator_runs WHERE subaccount_id=$1 AND status='running' AND superseded_by_attempt IS NULL`. To serialise slot accounting against concurrent dispatchers, each dispatch transaction first acquires `pg_advisory_xact_lock(hashtext('operator_slots:' || subaccount_id))`, then runs the count, then inserts the chain-link row. The lock is released at COMMIT. `SELECT count(*) ... FOR UPDATE` is insufficient on its own because aggregate counts do not lock the absence of rows.
625:
626:   - **New user-requested operator task over the cap:** REJECTED at task-create / first-dispatch with typed error `OPERATOR_SESSION_LIMIT_EXCEEDED`. Customer-facing message surfaced via the existing task-create / operator-capacity modal (canonical component path chosen by the implementation chunk; the mockup `r8-modal-concurrency-limit.html` documents the intended pattern). NOT queued. NOT an incident.
627:   - **Existing chain-continuation hitting the cap mid-task:** QUEUED FIFO on the new `'operator-session-dispatch-next-chain-link'` pg-boss queue. Task state stays `paused_for_chain_continuation`. Dispatched when a slot frees. NOT an incident â€” normal flow control.
628:
629:   **Slot-free wake-up mechanism.** After every chain-link finalise (terminal `completed | failed | cancelled`), the finaliser calls `operatorChainSchedulerService.releaseSlotAndEnqueueNext(subaccountId)`. Under the same `pg_advisory_xact_lock(hashtext('operator_slots:' || subaccount_id))` used at dispatch (Â§ 7.1 step 3), the scheduler scans the oldest `paused_for_chain_continuation` task for that subaccount whose pending `'operator-session-dispatch-next-chain-link'` job has been throttled by the cap, and enqueues exactly one new dispatch job for the freed slot. If multiple tasks are queued, the FIFO order is `agent_runs.updated_at ASC` for tasks in `paused_for_chain_continuation`. The pure helper for the scan/order lives in `operatorChainSchedulerServicePure.ts` (Â§ 5.1) and is unit-tested per Â§ 12.
630:
631:   The distinction matters: new tasks fail-fast so the user can address the cap immediately; in-flight tasks defer so a busy moment doesn't kill long-running work.
632:

codex

Standard org+subaccount scoping via the existing `current_setting('app.organisation_id')` and `current_setting('app.subaccount_id')` GUCs. `FORCE ROW LEVEL SECURITY` enabled (defeats owner-bypass). 1088:| **Route guard** | Reads go through `GET /api/operator-sessions/:operatorRunId/progress` â€” guards: `authenticate`, `requirePermission('AGENT_RUN_READ')`, and `setOrgGUC()` before the query. Direct-DB-access prohibition is enforced by `verify-rls-contract-compliance.sh`. |
1089:| **Principal-scoped context** | The adapter's `dispatch()`/`finalise()` run inside the existing agent-execution principal context (`PrincipalContext`). The chain-link writer uses `withOrgTx` for every write, propagating the org GUC. |

1115:
1116:- **`SUBACCOUNT_OPERATOR_SETTINGS_WRITE`** â€” granted by default to `org_admin`. Used only by the PATCH route. The implementation chunk adds the key to the permissions registry, the role-default grant, and the permission-coverage CI gate.

1118:### 6.5b Backend route guards for the new task-action routes
1119:
1120:All routes in `server/routes/operatorTasks.ts` (Â§ 5.1) MUST mount under `authenticate`, resolve the agent run + subaccount, call `setOrgGUC()`, and enforce a route-specific actor rule before mutating state. Actor rules match Â§ 6.6 UI gates:
1121:
1122:| Route | Actor rule | Permission key |
1123:|---|---|---|
1124:| `POST /api/operator-tasks/:agentRunId/retry-chain-failure` | assigned user OR `manager`+ | `AGENT_RUN_WRITE` (existing) |
1125:| `POST /api/operator-tasks/:agentRunId/extend-budget` | assigned user OR `manager`+ | `AGENT_RUN_WRITE` (existing) |
1126:| `POST /api/operator-tasks/:agentRunId/refresh-credential` | `org_admin` only | `AGENT_RUN_ADMIN` (existing) |
1127:| `POST /api/operator-tasks/:agentRunId/fresh-profile-restart` | `org_admin` only | `AGENT_RUN_ADMIN` (existing) |
1128:| `POST /api/operator-tasks/:agentRunId/extend-debug-retention` | `org_admin` only | `AGENT_RUN_ADMIN` (existing) |
1129:
1130:The `manager+` / assigned-user rule is enforced in the route handler (not by a single permission key) because the underlying state transitions are user-initiated lifecycle actions, not admin operations. The route handler reads `agent_runs.assigned_user_id` and `users.role` before authorising.
