1144:### 6.7 Tenant-isolation invariants (defence in depth)
1145:
1146:1. **Three-way subaccount match** at chain-link start: `task.subaccount_id == credential.subaccount_id == profile.subaccount_id`. Mismatch â†’ hard fail + incident.
1147:2. **No cross-tenant adapter calls** â€” `operatorManagedBackend.dispatch()` reads `agent_runs.subaccount_id` once, sets the GUC via `setOrgGUC()`, and uses the same scoped tx for every subsequent read/write within the chain link.
1148:3. **`operator_runs.organisation_id` AND `subaccount_id` are redundant with the FK chain** but kept on the row for RLS performance â€” Postgres applies the policy via these columns without a join.
1149:4. **The pg-boss handlers re-read** the org/subaccount from the row they're processing and re-establish the GUC before any tenant-scoped write (the queue payload carries `operator_run_id`; the handler resolves the rest).
1150:5. **The polling route** subaccount-checks via `setOrgGUC` + `getOrgScopedDb`; a row whose `subaccount_id` doesn't match the caller's principal returns 404 (NOT 403, to avoid leaking existence â€” consistent with the existing IEE route).
1151:

 succeeded in 744ms:
1152:## 7. Execution model
1153:
1154:Per `docs/spec-authoring-checklist.md Â§ 5`, one model is picked explicitly and the rest of the spec is consistent with it.
1155:
1156:### 7.1 Adapter `dispatch()` â€” inline / synchronous (chain-link start)
1157:
1158:The adapter's `dispatch()` call is **inline**: the caller (Spec A's dispatch orchestrator) waits for it to return. `dispatch()` does:
1159:
1160:1. Read `agent_runs` for `(organisation_id, subaccount_id)`.
1161:2. Set the GUC; resolve effective caps (`subaccountOperatorSettingsService.getEffectiveSettings(subaccountId)`).
1162:3. Concurrency-cap check. Acquire `pg_advisory_xact_lock(hashtext('operator_slots:' || subaccount_id))` inside the dispatch tx; then `count(*) FROM operator_runs WHERE subaccount_id=$1 AND status='running' AND superseded_by_attempt IS NULL`; then proceed with the `operator_runs` INSERT under the same lock (released at COMMIT). Plain `SELECT ... FOR UPDATE` is insufficient â€” aggregate counts do not lock absent rows (Â§ 10.3). If new task hitting cap â†’ throw `OPERATOR_SESSION_LIMIT_EXCEEDED` (NOT queued, per Â§ 3.17 item 5). If chain-continuation hitting cap â†’ return a structured response that the chain-resume dispatcher handles by re-queueing (FIFO).
1163:4. Three-way subaccount match (Â§ 6.7).
1164:5. Resolve credential via `credentialBrokerService.requestOperatorSessionCredential` (or `resolveFallback` if stickiness is set).
1165:6. Resolve / create profile via `operatorTaskProfileService.ensureActiveProfile(taskId, attemptNumber)`.
1166:7. Insert the `operator_runs` row (status `'pending'`).
1167:8. Call `sandboxExecutionService.runTask(...)` to start the sandbox session, injecting the credential and mounting the profile. The call MUST pass a `sandbox_start_key = operator_run_id` provider-side idempotency token so the sandbox provider can reject a duplicate start. The sandbox-isolation primitive supports this per Spec B.
1168:9. Receive the vendor session id; UPDATE the `operator_runs` row (status `'running'`, `started_at`, `vendor_session_id`).
1169:10. Return `BackendDispatchResult` with `backendTaskId = operatorRun.id`.
1170:
1171:**Dispatch-crash recovery (sandbox-orphan handling).** If `dispatch()` crashes between steps 7 and 9 â€” `operator_runs` row exists with `status='pending'` but `vendor_session_id IS NULL` â€” a retry of the same dispatch attempts adoption:
1172:
1173:1. Re-read the row; if `status='pending'` AND `vendor_session_id IS NULL`, call `sandboxExecutionService.adoptOrStart({ sandbox_start_key: operator_run_id, ... })` (the sandbox primitive returns the existing sandbox if one was created under that token, otherwise starts a fresh one).
1174:2. On adoption success: UPDATE `operator_runs SET status='running', started_at, vendor_session_id`.
1175:3. On adoption failure or ambiguous state: UPDATE `operator_runs SET status='failed', failure_reason='sandbox_start_unknown'` and emit `operator.chain_link_start_failed` per Â§ 3.17.
1176:
1177:The `sandbox_start_key = operator_run_id` discipline gives the system exactly-once sandbox creation per chain-link row even when `dispatch()` is retried after a crash. Without it, a retry produces a duplicate sandbox + an orphan billing path.
1178:
1179:A failure at any step (3â€“10) writes the chain-link row with status `'failed'` (or aborts before insert), emits the `operator.chain_link_start_failed` incident per Â§ 3.17, and the chain-link dispatcher (Â§ 7.3) handles retry/backoff.
1180:
1181:### 7.2 Chain-link terminal event â€” queued (pg-boss)
1182:
1183:When the sandbox session terminates (operator runtime emits a terminal step-state OR hard cap is reached OR cancel propagated OR runtime crashed), the adapter writes the chain-link row to its terminal status and enqueues `'operator-session-completed'` with payload `{ operatorRunId, agentRunId }`.
1184:
1185:The handler `operatorSessionCompletedHandler.ts`:
1186:
1187:1. Reads the `operator_runs` row (and its `checkpoint_payload`).
1188:2. Calls `finaliseAgentRunFromBackend({ backendId: 'operator_managed', backendTaskId: operatorRunId })`.
1189:3. Inside `finalise()`: the adapter decides task-terminal vs paused-for-continuation (per Â§ 3.14 item 4).
1190:4. If task-terminal: parent agent run rolls up; cost rows are written via `operatorCostWriter.writeRowsForChainLink(operatorRunId)`; profile is scheduled for GC.
1191:5. If paused-for-continuation: parent agent run sets `status='paused_for_chain_continuation'`; cost rows for THIS chain link are written via the same writer (per-chain-link cost rows happen regardless of pause/terminal); the chain-resume dispatcher enqueues `'operator-session-dispatch-next-chain-link'` with payload `{ agentRunId }`.
1192:
1193:**Idempotency posture (per Â§ 10.1):** key-based on `(operator_run_id, status)`. A re-delivery of the queue message is a no-op â€” the finaliser sees the row already in terminal state and returns the prior result.
1194:
1195:### 7.3 Chain-link dispatch â€” queued (pg-boss) with backoff retry
1196:
1197:`operatorSessionDispatchNextChainLinkHandler.ts`:
1198:
1199:1. Reads the parent `agent_runs` row.
1200:2. Proceed only when ALL of the following hold:
1201:   - `agent_runs.status` is one of `'pending'` (first dispatch â€” bootstrap path), `'paused_for_chain_continuation'`, `'paused_chain_failure'` (after user-initiated retry, counter has been reset), or `'paused_budget_exceeded'` (after user-initiated extension). NOTE: `'delegated'` is intentionally excluded â€” a `'delegated'` task already has a chain link in flight, and dispatching another would race.
1202:   - The queued-job reason tag matches the current paused-state resume action (`'continuation'` â†” `paused_for_chain_continuation`; `'retry'` â†” `paused_chain_failure`; `'budget_extension'` â†” `paused_budget_exceeded`; `'bootstrap'` â†” `pending`).
1203:   - `NOT EXISTS (SELECT 1 FROM operator_runs WHERE agent_run_id = $1 AND attempt_number = $2 AND status IN ('pending','running'))` â€” there is no in-flight chain link for the current attempt.
1204:   Otherwise no-op (idempotent re-delivery).
1205:3. Calls `executionBackendRegistry.get('operator_managed').dispatch({ agentRunId, ... })` â€” re-uses Â§ 7.1 inline path.
1206:4. On success: writes `agent_runs.status='delegated'` via the optimistic predicate `UPDATE agent_runs SET status='delegated', operator_chain_failure_count=0 WHERE id=$1 AND status IN ('pending','delegated','paused_for_chain_continuation','paused_chain_failure','paused_budget_exceeded')`. 0 rows-affected means the task is in a terminal state â€” no-op.
1207:5. On failure with `'transient'` failure class: increments `agent_runs.operator_chain_failure_count` (per Â§ 3.4 writer rules â€” predicate `UPDATE ... WHERE status IN ('delegated','paused_for_chain_continuation')`); enqueues a delayed re-dispatch (1 min â†’ 5 min â†’ 15 min via pg-boss's `startAfter` parameter).
1208:6. On the 3rd consecutive failure: writes `agent_runs.status='paused_chain_failure'`, emits `'operator-session.task_paused_chain_failure'` event, sends user notification.
1209:7. On failure with `'permanent' | 'auth' | 'profile_corruption'` failure class: bypasses the backoff and goes directly to `paused_chain_failure`.
1210:8. Every failure (transient or permanent) emits an `operator.chain_link_start_failed` incident with `retry_attempt` and `is_terminal`.
1211:
1212:**Idempotency posture:** key-based on `(agentRunId, attempt_number, chain_seq_next)`. `chain_seq_next` is computed as `max(chain_seq) + 1` **within the current `attempt_number`** (NOT across attempts â€” fresh-profile restart restarts chain_seq at 1 for the new attempt per Â§ 3.15 item 7). Re-delivery of the queue message is a no-op when the chain link is already in `pending`/`running`/terminal state at that `(attempt_number, chain_seq_next)`.
1213:
1214:### 7.4 Progress events â€” queued (pg-boss) + WebSocket bridge
1215:
1216:Step-boundary events from the operator runtime are enqueued (`'operator-session-progressed'`) to keep the runtime's hot path off the DB. `operatorSessionProgressedHandler.ts` is the **sole writer** for `operator_runs.last_progress_at` and `step_count`:
1217:
1218:1. `UPDATE operator_runs SET last_progress_at = greatest(coalesce(last_progress_at, '-infinity'::timestamptz), $event_timestamp), step_count = greatest(step_count, $step_index) WHERE id = $operator_run_id AND status = 'running'`. The `status = 'running'` guard enforces the Â§ 10.4 post-terminal prohibition: progress events arriving after the chain link reached terminal state update zero rows and are dropped. The `coalesce(..., '-infinity'::timestamptz)` makes the `greatest()` NULL-safe for the first event when `last_progress_at` is still NULL. `greatest()` on `step_count` (with NOT NULL default 0) is naturally safe.
1219:2. If step 1 updated 0 rows: log the drop and return (no WebSocket emission). Otherwise emit `'operator-session.progressed'` to the `agent-run:{runId}` WebSocket room via `emitAgentRunUpdate`.
1220:
1221:The WebSocket bridge is best-effort: a dropped event is acceptable (the next event picks up the state). The polling fallback route is the durable visibility path.
1222:
1223:### 7.5 Profile GC â€” queued (pg-boss cron)
1224:
1225:`operatorTaskProfileGcHandler.ts` is a 15-minute cron job that scans for `(status='scheduled_gc' AND scheduled_gc_at <= now())` rows, marks them `'gc_in_progress'`, deletes the underlying sandbox volume via the sandbox provider, then sets `'gc_done'`. The scan is system-wide.
1226:
1227:`operator_task_profiles` has `FORCE ROW LEVEL SECURITY` (Â§ 6.2), so the cron CANNOT use the default `db` handle (it would fail-closed with 0 rows on every UPDATE â€” the same pattern as `workflowDraftsCleanupJob`, `llmLedgerArchiveJob`, and the agent-run cleanup job). The handler MUST follow the existing cross-org maintenance pattern from `architecture.md` Â§ *Row-Level Security â€” Three-Layer Fail-Closed Data Isolation* / Â§ *Admin-bypass RLS*:
1228:
1229:```
1230:await withAdminConnection({ source: 'operatorTaskProfileGc' }, async (tx) => {
1231:  await tx.execute(sql`SET LOCAL ROLE admin_role`);
1232:  // scan + update + delete here
1233:});
1234:```
1235:
1236:`admin_role` carries `BYPASSRLS`; every invocation is logged to `audit_events` by `withAdminConnection`.
1237:
1238:**Idempotency:** key-based on `(profile_id, scheduled_gc_at)`. A re-run of the cron during deletion picks up only rows still in `'scheduled_gc'`; rows transitioned to `'gc_in_progress'` are skipped â€” EXCEPT for the stale-reclaim rule below.
1239:
1240:**Stale `'gc_in_progress'` reclaim.** A crash during volume deletion can strand a row in `'gc_in_progress'` forever. `operator_task_profiles` includes `gc_started_at timestamptz NULL` (set when the row transitions to `'gc_in_progress'`, cleared on transition to `'gc_done'`). The GC handler reclaims any row where `status='gc_in_progress' AND gc_started_at < now() - INTERVAL '30 minutes'` by treating it as eligible for a fresh deletion attempt. Provider HTTP 404 on the delete call is treated as success (volume already gone) and transitions the row to `'gc_done'`.
1241:
1242:### 7.6 Cost-writer â€” inline within finaliser transaction
1243:
1244:The cost-writer is **NOT a separate queue**. It runs inline within the `finalise()` transaction triggered by `'operator-session-completed'`. The terminal `status` on `operator_runs` was written by the adapter at chain-link end (Â§ 7.2). The finaliser does NOT re-set the terminal status; it commits the cost rows together with stamping `operator_runs.event_emitted_at = now()` so that "cost rows written" and "terminal event acknowledged" land atomically. This avoids the "event acknowledged but no cost row" or "cost row but event still un-acknowledged" partial state.
1245:
1246:If the cost-writer fails inside the finaliser: the transaction rolls back, `event_emitted_at` stays NULL, and the pg-boss queue retries delivery. The cost-writer's own idempotency (key-based on `(operator_run_id, source_type, boundary)`) ensures the retry doesn't double-write. The chain-link `status` itself was already committed by the adapter and is not affected by the rollback.
1247:
1248:### 7.7 No new feature flags
1249:
1250:Per framing (`spec-context.md`): `feature_flags: only_for_behaviour_modes`. The adapter registers unconditionally at boot. No `ENABLE_OPERATOR_BACKEND` flag. If the operator-session credential is unavailable for any subaccount, the existing connection-status surfaces the state.
1251:
1252:## 8. Phase plan
1253:
1254:Single phase. **Phase 1** ships the whole Operator Backend end-to-end as defined here. The brief's D8 (chain-resume required, not a phase-3.5 deferral) and D11 (persistent profile required, not deferred) are honoured: no sub-phase splits the model.
1255:
1256:| Item | Verdict | Notes |
1257:|---|---|---|
1258:| Operator Backend (`operator_managed`) end-to-end | **BUILD IN PHASE 1** | This spec; chunks 1â€“15 in Â§ 14. |
1259:| `operator_external` BYO compute adapter | **DEFER** to Phase 5 | Type slot reserved; no registration. |
1260:| Cross-provider session identity (Anthropic, Google) | **DEFER** to Phase 3.5 | Spec C `provider` field is forward-compat; V1 single-provider. |
1261:| Streaming progress as first-class | **DEFER** to Phase 3.5 | V1 keeps polling as visibility primitive. |
1262:| Manual checkpoint controls | **DEFER** to Phase 3.5 (D12) | V1 chain-resume is fully automatic. |
1263:
1264:The implementation chunks in Â§ 14 are sequential within Phase 1 but they are NOT phases â€” they are build-order ordering only. Each chunk leaves the system in a forward-compatible state (e.g. schema changes ship before the writers that depend on them).
1265:
1266:**Out-of-phase deferrals** (Phase 3.5 / Phase 5) are listed in Â§ 11.

1268:## 9. Phase sequencing (dependency graph)
1269:
1270:There is one phase, so phase-level sequencing is trivially satisfied. The chunk-level dependency graph in Â§ 14 has been checked against the three failure modes from `docs/spec-authoring-checklist.md Â§ 6`:
1271:
1272:1. **No backward dependency.** Every column referenced by code in Chunk N is created in an equal-or-earlier chunk's migration. Verified via the dependency table in Â§ 14.
1273:2. **No orphaned deferrals.** Every "deferred" item is listed in Â§ 11. Cross-checked.
1274:3. **No phase-boundary contradiction.** Only one phase; no boundary.

1278:## 10. Execution-safety contracts
1279:
1280:### 10.1 Idempotency posture (per write path)
1281:
1282:| Write path | Posture | Key |
1283:|---|---|---|
1284:| `operator_runs` insert (chain-link start) | **state-based** | optimistic predicate: `INSERT ... WHERE NOT EXISTS (SELECT 1 FROM operator_runs WHERE agent_run_id=$1 AND attempt_number=$2 AND chain_seq=$3)`. 0 rows-affected = a concurrent dispatcher already started this chain link. UNIQUE `(agent_run_id, attempt_number, chain_seq)` per Â§ 3.3 is the DB-level backstop. |
1285:| `operator_runs` terminal UPDATE | **state-based** | optimistic predicate: `UPDATE ... WHERE status IN ('pending','running')`. 0 rows-affected = already terminal. |
1286:| `agent_runs` terminal UPDATE to `completed` or `failed` | **state-based** | optimistic predicate: `UPDATE ... WHERE status='delegated'`. A paused task MUST transition `delegated` first (re-dispatch a chain link) before it can roll up to terminal `completed`/`failed`. 0 rows-affected = already terminal OR still paused; finaliser logs and returns 200 idempotent-hit. |
1287:| `agent_runs` terminal UPDATE to `cancelled` | **state-based** | optimistic predicate: `UPDATE ... WHERE status IN ('pending','delegated','paused_for_chain_continuation','paused_chain_failure','paused_budget_exceeded')`. Any pre-terminal state may transition directly to `cancelled` (user cancel). 0 rows-affected = already terminal; return `409` with current state. |
1288:| `agent_runs` pause UPDATE (`paused_for_chain_continuation`) | **state-based** | optimistic predicate: `UPDATE ... WHERE status='delegated'`. 0 rows-affected = a concurrent path already paused or terminated. |
1289:| `operator_task_profiles` insert (first chain link) | **key-based** | unique constraint: `(task_id, attempt_number)`. 23505 â†’ catch and return the existing row (idempotent-hit). |
1290:| `subaccount_operator_settings` UPSERT | **key-based** | PK: `subaccount_id`. Conflict â†’ If-Match check (state-based concurrency control on top of key-based identity). |
1291:| `operator_runs` progress UPDATE (`last_progress_at`, `step_count`) | **key-based** | event key `(operator_run_id, step_index)`; the handler uses `greatest(last_progress_at, ...)` and `greatest(step_count, ...)` so duplicate / out-of-order deliveries are no-ops. The pg-boss enqueue carries the same singleton key. |
1292:| `llm_requests` cost rows | **key-based** | unique index: `(operator_run_id, source_type, boundary)` for the new rows (added by migration `0331`); existing `(agent_run_id, request_id)` for `per_token` rows. 23505 â†’ idempotent-hit. |
1293:| pg-boss `'operator-session-completed'` enqueue | **key-based** | pg-boss singleton key: `'operator-session-completed:' || operator_run_id`. Re-enqueue is a no-op. |
1294:| pg-boss `'operator-session-dispatch-next-chain-link'` enqueue | **key-based** | singleton key: `'operator-session-dispatch-next-chain-link:' || agent_run_id || ':' || attempt_number || ':' || chain_seq_next`. |
1295:| pg-boss `'operator-task-profile-gc'` cron tick | **state-based** | the cron handler's `UPDATE WHERE status='scheduled_gc' AND scheduled_gc_at <= now() RETURNING id` is the eligibility predicate; concurrent ticks see disjoint row sets. |
1296:| Audit-event write | **non-idempotent (intentional)** | every action records its own audit row; replays are intentional duplicates so the audit log captures every attempted-action. |
1297:
1298:### 10.2 Retry classification
1299:
1300:| Operation | Classification | Notes |
1301:|---|---|---|
1302:| `credentialBrokerService.requestOperatorSessionCredential` | **guarded** | broker enforces its own idempotency; safe to retry on network errors. |
1303:| `sandboxExecutionService.runTask` | **guarded** | the `sandbox_start_key = operator_run_id` token (Â§ 7.1) gives the provider exactly-once semantics. On retry: `sandboxExecutionService.adoptOrStart()` either adopts the existing sandbox under the token or starts a fresh one. Without the token a retry would orphan the prior sandbox. |
1304:| `operatorCostWriter.writeRowsForChainLink` | **safe** | key-based idempotent. Retry is a no-op. |
1305:| `recordIncident` | **safe** | Spec C / existing pattern â€” incident ingestor is internally idempotent. |
1306:| WebSocket emission `emitAgentRunUpdate` | **safe** | best-effort; loss is acceptable. |
1307:| `operatorSessionDispatchNextChainLinkHandler` | **guarded** | wrapped by `operator_runs` (chain_seq) idempotency. |
1308:| `operatorTaskProfileGcHandler` | **guarded** | row-state predicate prevents double-delete. |
1309:| Profile-volume `delete` (Spec B provider call) | **unsafe** | a retry against a missing volume must be treated as success (the provider returns 404 â†’ treat as `gc_done`). Wrapped by `operator_task_profiles.status` predicate. |
1310:
1311:### 10.3 Concurrency guards
1312:
1313:| Race | Guard |
1314:|---|---|
1315:| Two concurrent chain-link dispatchers for the same task | `operator_runs (agent_run_id, attempt_number, chain_seq)` UNIQUE + `INSERT ... WHERE NOT EXISTS` keyed on the same triple. First wins; second gets 0 rows-affected and re-queries to see the winner's row, then no-ops. |
1316:| Two concurrent task-cancel callers | `agent_runs` UPDATE with optimistic predicate on the pre-terminal closed set. First wins; second gets 0 rows-affected and returns 409 with the current state. |
1317:| Two concurrent dispatches racing past the concurrency cap | `pg_advisory_xact_lock(hashtext('operator_slots:' || subaccount_id))` inside the dispatch tx; the lock serialises all dispatchers for the same subaccount. The count then runs against `operator_runs WHERE subaccount_id=$1 AND status='running' AND superseded_by_attempt IS NULL`. The lock is released at COMMIT. Plain `SELECT count(*) FOR UPDATE` is insufficient â€” aggregate counts don't lock absent rows. |
1318:| Two concurrent settings-PATCH calls | optimistic concurrency on `updated_at`. Second caller's `If-Match` mismatches â†’ 409. |
1319:| Two concurrent finalises for the same chain link | the finaliser's `operator_runs` UPDATE optimistic predicate gives one winner. The cost-writer's key-based idempotency gives second a no-op. |
1320:| Cron GC + admin debug-retention | the GC scan reads `scheduled_gc_at`; if an admin extends retention between scan and update, the row's `scheduled_gc_at` moves forward AND the cron's UPDATE-WHERE predicate (`status='scheduled_gc' AND scheduled_gc_at <= now()`) returns 0 rows on the second pass. Safe. |
1321:| Fresh-profile-restart racing in-flight chain link | the restart route requires the task to be in a paused state. Optimistic predicate: `UPDATE agent_runs SET ... WHERE status IN ('paused_chain_failure','paused_budget_exceeded','paused_for_chain_continuation')`. Terminal `failed | completed | cancelled` is never restarted under the same `agent_run_id` (Â§ 10.7 forbidden transitions). A `running`/`delegated` chain link blocks restart. |
1322:
1323:### 10.4 Terminal event guarantees
1324:
1325:**Chain-link terminal events** (one per chain link):
1326:
1327:- Exactly one of `'operator-session.chain_link_completed' | '.chain_link_failed' | '.chain_link_cancelled'` per chain link.
1328:- Post-terminal prohibition: no further events with the same `chain_link_id` after a terminal event. **Exception:** `'operator-session.artefact_harvested'` (Â§ 4.7) is allowed to fire AFTER the chain-link terminal event only because artefact harvest can complete asynchronously to the chain-link finalise. When `artefact_harvested` fires post-terminal, its payload MUST omit `chain_link_id` and reference the task by `agent_run_id` only. When it fires pre-terminal (the common case), it carries `chain_link_id`. The harvest writer decides which form based on whether the chain link is still `'running'` at harvest time.
1329:- The terminal event's `status` is `'completed'` (with checkpoint OR final), `'failed'`, or `'cancelled'`. No `'partial'` at the chain-link level â€” partial completion of a chain link IS a `'completed'` with checkpoint (which is the normal case for non-final links).
1330:
1331:**Task terminal events** (one per task, only on true terminal states):
1332:
1333:- Exactly one of `'operator-session.task_completed' | '.task_failed' | '.task_cancelled'` per task.
1334:- Post-terminal prohibition: no further events with the same `agent_run_id` after a terminal event.
1335:- Paused states emit `'operator-session.task_paused_*'` events; they are NOT terminal â€” multiple may fire over a task's life (pause â†’ resume â†’ pause â†’ resume â†’ terminal).
1336:- **Single-writer guard.** Before emitting any `operator-session.task_*` terminal event, the writer MUST acquire the singleton key `operator-session-task-terminal:${agent_run_id}` (via pg-boss singleton enqueue OR via an `INSERT INTO task_terminal_event_guard (agent_run_id) ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING RETURNING ...` write â€” implementation chunk picks one mechanism). The first writer that acquires the key emits; subsequent writers (e.g. a racing finaliser after a user cancel won the `agent_runs` UPDATE) see the conflict and no-op. This guarantees exactly one task-terminal event per task even when cancel and finaliser race.
1337:
1338:### 10.5 No-silent-partial-success
1339:
1340:Every flow that can partially complete emits an explicit status. Concretely:
1341:
1342:- A chain link that started but didn't finish a task â†’ `'chain_link_completed'` with checkpoint (NOT silent partial).
1343:- A task that hit the budget cap mid-chain-link â†’ the chain link `'chain_link_completed'` with checkpoint; the task `'task_paused_budget_exceeded'` (NOT a silent partial on the task).
1344:- A task that exhausted max chain length â†’ `'task_failed'` with `failure_reason='max_chain_length_reached'` (NOT silent).
1345:- A fallback-engaged chain link â†’ mixed cost rows per Â§ 3.12; both row types reflect the boundary explicitly.
1346:
1347:### 10.6 Unique-constraint â†’ HTTP status mapping
1348:
1349:| Constraint | Violated when | HTTP status |
1350:|---|---|---|
1351:| `operator_runs (agent_run_id, attempt_number, chain_seq) UNIQUE` | Concurrent dispatch race | (internal â€” converted by `INSERT ... WHERE NOT EXISTS` to 0-rows; no HTTP exposure) |
1352:| `operator_task_profiles (task_id, attempt_number) UNIQUE` | Concurrent ensure-profile | 23505 caught, idempotent-hit, returns existing row body to caller. (Internal route's HTTP equivalent: 200 idempotent.) |
1353:| `subaccount_operator_settings (subaccount_id) PK` | UPSERT conflict | normal UPSERT semantics (no HTTP exposure). |
1354:| `llm_requests (operator_run_id, source_type, boundary) UNIQUE` (new) | Cost-writer retry | 23505 caught, idempotent-hit, returns 200. |
1355:| `subaccount_operator_settings` If-Match mismatch | Stale write | 409 `OPERATOR_SETTINGS_CONFLICT` with `current_state` in body. |
1356:| Cancel a task already in terminal state | optimistic predicate 0 rows | 409 `TASK_ALREADY_TERMINAL` with `current_status` in body. |
1357:| Fresh-profile-restart on running chain link | optimistic predicate 0 rows | 409 `OPERATOR_TASK_RESTART_BLOCKED` with `current_status` and `active_chain_link_id` in body. |
1358:| New operator task over concurrency cap | computed at dispatch | 429 `OPERATOR_SESSION_LIMIT_EXCEEDED` with `cap`, `current`, `subaccount_id` in body. |
1359:
1360:No `23505` is allowed to bubble as a 500. The typed exception classes â€” `OperatorBackendConflictError` for 409 cases and `OperatorSessionLimitExceededError` for 429 â€” live in `server/services/operatorBackendErrors.ts` (Â§ 5.1). They are mapped to the HTTP statuses above by the existing route error-handler middleware (the same one already mapping `ZodError` and the other typed-error classes); the build chunk wires the case clauses, no new mapper file is introduced.
1361:
1362:### 10.7 State machine closures (`operator_runs`, `agent_runs`)
1363:
1364:**`operator_runs.status` enum is CLOSED.** Adding a new value requires a spec amendment.
1365:
1366:Valid transitions:
1367:
1368:```
1369:pending â†’ running          (sandbox session created, vendor_session_id populated)
1370:pending â†’ failed           (dispatch failure â€” auth, profile, runtime unavailable)
1371:pending â†’ cancelled        (user cancelled before sandbox started)
1372:running â†’ completed        (operator runtime terminal-success OR checkpoint-ready)
1373:running â†’ failed           (operator runtime crash OR heartbeat stale OR auth lost without fallback OR hard-cap unresumable)
1374:running â†’ cancelled        (user cancelled mid-link OR task-level cancel propagated)
1375:```
1376:
1377:Forbidden:
1378:- Any transition from `completed | failed | cancelled` (terminal).
1379:- `pending â†’ completed` (a chain link MUST be `running` before it can complete â€” there is no "skip the runtime" path).
1380:- `pending â†’ cancelled` from heartbeat-stale (cannot have a stale heartbeat without a running sandbox).
1381:
1382:**`agent_runs.status` enum is CLOSED** (the Operator-Backend-relevant subset; the full enum is broader and pre-existing).
1383:
1384:Valid transitions (operator-managed paths only):
1385:
1386:```
1387:pending â†’ delegated                                  (first chain dispatch)
1388:delegated â†’ paused_for_chain_continuation            (chain link completed with checkpoint, task not done)
1389:paused_for_chain_continuation â†’ delegated            (next chain link dispatched)
1390:delegated â†’ paused_chain_failure                     (3 consecutive dispatch failures)
1391:paused_chain_failure â†’ delegated                     (user retried)
1392:delegated â†’ paused_budget_exceeded                   (budget cap hit)
1393:paused_budget_exceeded â†’ delegated                   (user extended budget)
1394:delegated â†’ completed                                (final chain link task_completed)
1395:delegated â†’ failed                                   (operator runtime hard error OR max chain length)
1396:delegated â†’ paused_chain_failure                     (hard-cap unresumable: running chain link with failed_mid_step=true per Â§ 3.14 item 3; counted in the same dispatch-failure budget as start failures)
1397:{pending | delegated | paused_*} â†’ cancelled         (user cancelled)
1398:```
1399:
1400:Forbidden:
1401:- Any transition from `completed | failed | cancelled` (terminal).
1402:- `pending â†’ completed | failed` without going through `delegated` (operator-managed tasks must enter delegation first before completion or failure). **`pending â†’ cancelled` IS permitted** â€” a user may cancel a task before its first chain-link dispatch.
1403:- `paused_* â†’ completed | failed` without re-entering `delegated` (a paused task MUST resume to dispatch a chain link before it can produce a task-terminal `completed`/`failed` status). **`paused_* â†’ cancelled` IS permitted** at any time (user cancel from a paused state).
1404:
1405:Enforcement: optimistic predicates on every writer (Â§ 10.1, Â§ 10.3). No DB-level CHECK on transition graph (Postgres doesn't support state-machine constraints declaratively); the writer-level predicates are the enforcement.
1406:
1407:**Adding a new status value:** any future spec adding to either enum MUST:
1408:1. Add the value to the migration AND the union/type-annotation in the schema file.
1409:2. Update this spec's state-machine diagrams (or supersede this spec).
1410:3. Update every writer's optimistic predicates.
1411:4. Update the UI status-pill renderer.
1412:

 succeeded in 766ms:
1413:## 11. Deferred items
1414:
1415:Single source of truth. Every "deferred", "later", "future", "Phase 3.5", "Phase 5" reference in this spec corresponds to a line below.
1416:
1417:- **DEFER â€” `operator_external` adapter registration.** Type slot reserved; no runtime registration in V1. Phase 5 â€” BYO compute / customer-hosted operator workers.
1418:- **DEFER â€” Cross-provider session identity (Anthropic Claude.ai, Google Gemini).** Spec C's `provider` field is forward-compat; V1 only registers the ChatGPT-Plus operator-session provider. Phase 3.5.
1419:- **DEFER â€” Routing policy / cost-aware dispatch between Operator Backend and Native adapters.** Phase 3.5 â€” separate spec.
1420:- **DEFER â€” "Cost savings vs API" customer-facing dashboard.** Phase 3.5. V1 surfaces cost in existing usage views only.
1421:- **DEFER â€” Streaming progress as first-class capability.** Phase 3.5 â€” V1 keeps polling as the visibility primitive.
1422:- **DEFER â€” Customer self-service tier switching UI.** Phase 3.5.
1423:- **DEFER â€” Manual checkpoint controls (user-triggered "checkpoint now").** Phase 3.5. D12 â€” chain-resume is entirely automatic in V1.
1424:- **DEFER â€” Predict-and-warn classifier for un-resumable flows at task-create time.** Phase 3.5. D7/Â§3.14 â€” best-effort with auto-extend grace is V1 policy.
1425:- **DEFER â€” Operator session export/import to external infrastructure.** Phase 5. V1 keeps all chain links inside the managed Operator Backend.
1426:- **DEFER â€” Per-subaccount profile-size-cap configuration.** V1 has a system-wide 500 MB constant (Â§ 3.15 item 3). If customer demand surfaces, future spec adds it to `subaccount_operator_settings`.
1427:- **DEFER â€” Cross-attempt comparison view in Run Trace.** Â§ 3.15 item 7 / Â§ 3.11 â€” V1 renders attempts as collapsed groups; a side-by-side compare view is deferred.
1428:- **DEFER â€” In-flight settings hot-application.** V1 snapshots caps at chain-link dispatch time; in-flight chain links use the snapshot. A future spec could push settings changes to a running chain link (the operator runtime would need a "soft re-cap" signal). Deferred â€” operationally complex, low demand.
1429:- **DEFER â€” In-memory slot-allocator cache** for concurrency-cap checks. V1 always queries the DB inside `pg_advisory_xact_lock(hashtext('operator_slots:' || subaccount_id))` (Â§ 7.1 step 3, Â§ 10.3); no in-memory slot allocator is permitted. A future optimisation could cache slot counts in Redis if hot-path performance becomes a concern. Deferred â€” premature.

1431:## 12. Testing posture
1432:
1433:Cross-referenced against [`docs/spec-context.md`](../../spec-context.md) and [`references/test-gate-policy.md`](../../../references/test-gate-policy.md).
1434:
1435:- **Static gates primary.** New CI gates (`scripts/gates/verify-execution-capability-references.sh`, `verify-operator-event-registry.sh`, `verify-no-checkpoint-logging.sh`) catch propagation drift and discipline violations.
1436:- **Pure-function tests authored alongside the code.** Pure helpers in `*Pure.ts` files get vitest pure-function tests (`*Pure.test.ts`) covering happy path + at least one edge case per branch. Pure helpers that matter most: state-mapping (chain-link â†’ task), retry-counter logic, settings snapshot extraction, idempotency-key derivation, profile-retention math, fallback-stickiness rules.
1437:- **RLS contract tests.** New tables added to `rlsProtectedTables.ts` are picked up by existing `verify-rls-coverage.sh` / `verify-rls-contract-compliance.sh` automatically. The existing `rls.context-propagation.test.ts` covers the default-deny posture â€” no new harness needed.
1438:- **No new frontend tests, no E2E, no API-contract tests.** Per `spec-context.md`: `frontend_tests: none_for_now`, `e2e_tests_of_own_app: none_for_now`, `api_contract_tests: none_for_now`.
1439:- **No new test runner.** Vitest only, per `docs/testing-conventions.md`.
1440:
1441:### 12.1 What's NOT tested at the runtime level
1442:
1443:Per the framing posture (rapid evolution, pre-production, no live customers), V1 does NOT include:
1444:
1445:- Runtime integration tests against a real sandbox provider.
1446:- Runtime smoke tests for the chain-resume flow end-to-end.
1447:- Load tests for the concurrency-cap accounting under contention.
1448:- Tests against the vendor operator runtime itself (vendor-side change risk is mitigated by the pinned `image_tag` + per-chain-link image discipline, not by a test).
1449:
1450:The first real Plus-tier customer pilot is the first integration test, by design. The brief's CS runbook (Â§ 3.13) is the operational mitigation.

### 7.2 Chain-link terminal event â€” queued (pg-boss)

When the sandbox session terminates (operator runtime emits a terminal step-state OR hard cap is reached OR cancel propagated OR runtime crashed), the adapter writes the chain-link row to its terminal status and enqueues 
 is insufficient on its own because aggregate counts do not lock the absence of rows.

   - **New user-requested operator task over the cap:** REJECTED at task-create / first-dispatch with typed error 
 IS permitted** at any time (user cancel from a paused state).

Enforcement: optimistic predicates on every writer (Â§ 10.1, Â§ 10.3). No DB-level CHECK on transition graph (Postgres doesn't support state-machine constraints declaratively); the writer-level predicates are the enforcement.

**Adding a new status value:** any future spec adding to either enum MUST:
1. Add the value to the migration AND the union/type-annotation in the schema file.
2. Update this spec's state-machine diagrams (or supersede this spec).
3. Update every writer's optimistic predicates.
4. Update the UI status-pill renderer.

## 1. Goals, non-goals, framing

### 1.1 What this spec ships

The first concrete autonomous-operator backend that consumes Spec A (adapter contract), Spec B (sandbox isolation), and Spec C (operator-session identity) end-to-end. After this lands, an operator-session subscription can drive long-form autonomous tasks inside a sandboxed runtime, with subscription-mediated cost in place of per-token API spend.

The customer-facing capability:

> Connect an operator-session subscription, run long-form autonomous tasks inside a sandboxed runtime, pay subscription-mediated cost instead of per-token API cost. Long tasks (hours to days) survive across many 120-minute chain-link sessions automatically; per-task limits are configured per subaccount.

export type ExecutionCapability =
  | 'in_process'
  | 'delegated'
  | 'subprocess'
  | 'browser_automation'
  | 'code_execution'
  | 'terminal_repo'
  | 'cancellation'
  | 'long_running'   // new in Spec D
  | 'session_identity'; // declared on operator_managed; non-gating at runtime in V1

156:The adapter declares capabilities `['delegated', 'code_execution', 'long_running', 'cancellation', 'session_identity']`.
158:Both `'long_running'` AND `'session_identity'` are **new** in this spec — added to `ExecutionCapability` at `server/services/executionBackends/types.ts:86-93`. (`'session_identity'` was referenced by Spec C but never added to the union there; this spec adds both literals in the same edit.) Both are declared on `operator_managed`; `'long_running'` gates chain-resume behaviour, `'session_identity'` is non-gating at runtime in V1. The propagation invariant has three rules:
161:2. **Zero ad-hoc literals in consumers.** A new CI gate (`scripts/gates/verify-execution-capability-references.sh`) greps the repo for any naked occurrence of the literal `'long_running'` outside the canonical definition. CI fails on a naked occurrence in any of: routes, services other than adapter objects, hooks, jobs, client code. **Permitted occurrences** (enumerated in the gate's allow-list):
162:   - The canonical definition in `server/services/executionBackends/types.ts`.
163:   - Adapter object declarations under `server/services/executionBackends/*.ts` (the literal is type-checked against the `ExecutionCapability` union at the declaration site — drift cannot occur silently).
165:   - Documentation, this spec, the brief, this gate's own script.
166:3. **Type-checker is the enforcement for adapter declarations.** Because adapter `capabilities` arrays are typed as `ExecutionCapability[]`, mistyping `'long_running'` as `'longrunning'` is a compile error. The CI gate covers the non-adapter consumer surface (routes, services, hooks, jobs, client code) where the literal would otherwise leak.

220:'pending' | 'running' | 'delegated' |
225:`'pending'`, `'running'`, `'delegated'`, `'completed'`, `'failed'`, `'cancelled'` already exist. **New** in this spec:
226:- `'paused_for_chain_continuation'` — scheduler-owned wait OR FIFO queue for next chain dispatch (§ 3.14, § 3.17).
230:**Task-terminal states are `completed | failed | cancelled` only.** The three `paused_*` states are resumable/non-terminal — they emit task-state-change events (UI updates, user notifications, scheduler suspension) but DO NOT trigger terminal artefact/cost finalisation. Cost rows for chain links that completed before the pause are written normally per § 3.12. The customer-visible terminal rollup is reserved for the true terminal states. Downstream consumers (cost dashboards, audit, evals) MUST NOT treat partial/pause-state rollups as final. See § 10.4 for the terminal-event guarantee.
232:A migration extends the existing `agent_runs.status` CHECK constraint (or text-typed allow-list, whichever the current schema uses). The migration is forward-compatible — existing status values are unchanged.
234:The same migration adds a new column `operator_chain_failure_count integer NOT NULL DEFAULT 0` to `agent_runs`. It counts **consecutive** chain-link dispatch failures since the last successful dispatch (per § 7.3 item 5). The chain-link dispatcher is the sole writer:
236:- Increment under `UPDATE agent_runs SET operator_chain_failure_count = operator_chain_failure_count + 1 WHERE id = $1 AND status IN ('delegated','paused_for_chain_continuation','paused_chain_failure','paused_budget_exceeded')`. The dispatcher's queued-job reason gate (§ 7.3 step 2) ensures retries from paused states are only counted when the queued reason matches the current paused-state resume action.
242:pending → delegated  (on first chain-link dispatch)
243:delegated → paused_for_chain_continuation  (on chain-link checkpoint terminal)
244:paused_for_chain_continuation → delegated  (on next chain-link dispatch)
245:delegated → paused_chain_failure  (on 3rd consecutive chain-link start failure)
246:paused_chain_failure → delegated  (on user-initiated retry)
247:delegated → paused_budget_exceeded  (on per-task budget cap hit)
248:paused_budget_exceeded → delegated  (on user budget extension)
249:delegated → completed | failed  (on task-terminal event from final chain link)
250:{pending | delegated | paused_*} → cancelled  (on user cancel)
253:Forbidden: any transition from a terminal state. Forbidden: `pending → completed` (a task MUST be delegated before terminating). The forbidden transitions are enforced by an optimistic predicate in the writer (see § 10.3).

284:   `ApiKeyEnvelope` is declared in `server/services/credentialBrokerService.ts` with shape `{ credentialId: string, connectionId: string, authType: 'api_key', provider: string, issuedAt: string, expiresAt: string | null }`. Raw API key material remains broker-internal and never leaves the broker — the adapter consumes the envelope reference (`credentialId`) only, mirroring the `OperatorSessionEnvelope` discipline. (Spec C reserved this seam; the spec author wires the broker side in the same chunk that wires the adapter side.)
302:   Both clearing signals (`operator-session.usability_restored` and `task.operator.credential_refreshed`) are looked up by querying the existing event/audit stores (already RLS-scoped to the task). 318:  3. The handler then bridges to the WebSocket `agent-run:{runId}` room via `emitAgentRunUpdate(runId, 'operator-session.progressed', payload)`.
320:- **Polling fallback (pull).** `GET /api/operator-sessions/:operatorRunId/progress` returns the latest progress snapshot from the `operator_runs` row. Route mirrors `server/routes/iee.ts:GET /api/iee/runs/:ieeRunId/progress`. Same auth gates: `authenticate`, `requirePermission('AGENT_RUN_READ')`, subaccount scoping via `getOrgScopedDb()`.
322:The polling route exists because (a) the WebSocket bridge can be down without the run being broken, and (b) some agent-run consumers don't keep a socket open. The brief is explicit that V1 keeps polling as the visibility primitive; streaming progress is deferred to Phase 3.5.
335:2. **Drain queued chain-continuation jobs** — remove FIFO-queued continuation entries (§ 3.17 item 5) for this task from the scheduler queue. Atomic with step 3.
336:3. **Prevent further chain dispatch** — set `agent_runs.status = 'cancelled'` via the optimistic predicate `UPDATE agent_runs SET status='cancelled' WHERE id = $1 AND status IN ('delegated','paused_for_chain_continuation','paused_chain_failure','paused_budget_exceeded','pending')`. 0 rows-affected means the task is already in a terminal state; return `409` with the current state.

364:One `source_type: 'sandbox_compute'` row per chain link / sandbox session. Inputs taken from Spec B's `SandboxRunTaskOutput`: `vCPUSeconds`, `wallClockMs`, `peakMemoryBytes`. Cost is computed by the existing sandbox-compute pricing function (Spec B). The ledger row carries the chain link's `operator_run_id` and is joined to the parent task at read time via `agent_run_id`.
370:Implementation note: the writer queries the lifecycle event store for `operator-session.fallback_engaged` for this `operator_run_id`; presence of such an event means the chain link DID start with `operator_session` regardless of the final column value, and `subscription_mediated` writes the pre-swap portion (`step_count` = `fallback_engaged.step_index`, by the cost-writer pure helper).
401:**Concurrency guard (per § 10.3):** the cost-writer holds an advisory lock on `(operator_run_id)` for the duration of the rollup transaction. Two concurrent finalises (rare; only possible if the pg-boss event handler retries before idempotency catches it) cannot interleave row writes.

The CS notification is the typed event `cs.operator_session.suspended_detected` produced by `notifyOperatorSessionSuspended()` (`server/services/operatorSessionSuspensionNotifier.ts`, § 5.1) and consumed by the existing inbox pipeline — no new pipeline component is introduced.

427:2. **Checkpoint contents (minimum).** § 4.6 pins the JSONB shape. 431:   - At `T - 10 min`, the operator emits a `'preparing_checkpoint'` step-state signal. The adapter enqueues an `operator-session-progressed` event with the step-state `preparing_checkpoint`; per § 3.9 / § 7.4, `operatorSessionProgressedHandler.ts` is the sole writer for `last_progress_at` and `step_count`. The handler bridges the state to the WebSocket room.
437:4. **Chain-link dispatch.** End of chain link N writes `checkpoint_payload` and emits `'operator-session-completed'` (the standard adapter terminal event, with status `'completed'` and a non-null `checkpoint_payload` field — distinct from the task-terminal `'completed'`). The finaliser handler distinguishes (branches evaluated in order; first match wins):
438:   - `completed` with non-null `checkpoint_payload` AND consumed-budget-minutes ≥ pinned `settings_snapshot.per_task_budget_cap_minutes` → task transitions to `'paused_budget_exceeded'`; do NOT enqueue the next chain link.
439:   - `completed` with non-null `checkpoint_payload` AND (`now() - first_operator_run.started_at`) ≥ pinned `settings_snapshot.max_wall_clock_per_task_days` → task transitions to `'paused_budget_exceeded'` with `failure_reason='max_wall_clock_exceeded'`; do NOT enqueue the next chain link.
441:   - `completed` with non-null `checkpoint_payload` (none of the above caps tripped) → dispatch next chain link via the `'operator-session-dispatch-next-chain-link'` queue.
444:   - `failed` with `failed_mid_step=false` → propagate task-terminal `'failed'` (operator runtime hard error, e.g. crash).
445:   - `cancelled` → propagate task-terminal `'cancelled'`.
449:6. **Conversation history accumulation.** Per-chain-link blobs joined at read time, capped at last N chain links of context for the operator-model invocation. Concretely: each chain link writes a single artefact `operator-conversation-link-{operator_run_id}.json` to the existing artefact store. The artefact's MIME type is `application/vnd.synthetos.operator-conversation-link+json;version=1` and its shape is the Zod schema `OperatorConversationLinkArtefact` declared in `shared/types/operatorConversationArtefact.ts` (a new file, § 5.1). The resume payload composer reads the latest K (default 5) artefacts and concatenates them in chain order. K is a constant in `operatorConversationHistoryPure.ts`; not configurable per-subaccount in V1.
453:   - **Hard-cap unresumable** (a specific running-state failure where soft-cap + grace elapsed without a checkpoint-safe state) is routed per § 3.14 item 3: chain link `'failed'` + `failed_mid_step=true`, task `paused_chain_failure`. It is NOT a hard runtime failure for the purposes of this classification.
464:10. **Checkpoint-payload security.** Checkpoint payloads are sensitive task artefacts and MUST be:
465:    - **Encrypted at rest** where existing artefact infrastructure supports it. Concretely: the JSONB column is written via the existing app-level encryption helper (the same helper used by `agent_run_payloads`'s redaction pipeline). The tentative file is `server/services/agentRunPayloadEncryptionService.ts` exporting `encryptAgentRunPayloadJson(value): Promise<EncryptedJson>` and `decryptAgentRunPayloadJson(value): Promise<unknown>`. If the in-tree names differ, Chunk 1 (or the chunk that first touches the checkpoint writer) MUST update this spec before implementation.
467:    - **Excluded from broad logs.** The adapter MUST NOT log `checkpoint_payload` contents at any log level. A grep gate (`scripts/gates/verify-no-checkpoint-logging.sh`) bans naive log calls referencing the column.
468:    - **Redacted in Run Trace by default.** The embedded screenshot is treated as an INTERNAL recovery artefact, not customer-visible. Customer-facing screenshots flow only through the harvested-artefact path (§ 3.12 / artefact harvester).
474:1. **Profile storage — new table `operator_task_profiles`.**
488:| `gc_started_at` | `timestamptz NULL` | Set on transition to `'gc_in_progress'`; cleared on transition to `'gc_done'`. The GC handler reclaims stale `'gc_in_progress'` rows (`gc_started_at < now() - INTERVAL '30 minutes'`) per § 7.5. |
503:4. **Profile lifecycle + retention.** Volume is created on first chain-link start (`status='active'`). Persists across chain links. After task-terminal: `status='scheduled_gc', scheduled_gc_at = now() + INTERVAL '48 hours'` (default). An admin (`org_admin`) may set `debug_retention_extended_by/_at` at task-terminal time, which extends `scheduled_gc_at` to `now() + INTERVAL '14 days'` for that task. Customer-visible artefacts (per § 3.12) are harvested into the artefact store BEFORE the volume is GC'd, regardless of retention window. A pg-boss cron job (`operator-task-profile-gc`, every 15 minutes) marks profiles `status='gc_in_progress'` when `now() >= scheduled_gc_at`, performs the volume delete via the sandbox provider, then sets `status='gc_done'`. Hard max lifetime including retention = `max_wall_clock_per_task_days` + 14 days.
558:**Defaulting.** When a chain link reads its caps and no row exists for the subaccount, the read uses the column defaults. The first write inserts the row (UPSERT pattern). No backfill migration is needed; the row is created lazily.
578:2. **Incident emission.** Each retry attempt writes its own incident via `recordIncident()` (`server/services/incidentIngestor.ts`). Typed event: `operator.chain_link_start_failed`. Idempotency key: `operator.chain_link_start_failed:${agent_run_id}:${attempt_number}:${chain_seq}:${retry_attempt}`. Pg-boss redelivery of the same retry attempt is a no-op. Payload (locked shape — § 4.8):
609:3. **User notification.** On `paused_chain_failure` transition, notify the assigned user via the existing inbox/notification path. Notification payload includes the failure class and the suggested action (Retry / Cancel). User actions:
624:   The `concurrent_operator_sessions_cap` per subaccount is computed at dispatch time as `count of operator_runs WHERE subaccount_id=$1 AND status='running' AND superseded_by_attempt IS NULL`. To serialise slot accounting against concurrent dispatchers, each dispatch transaction first acquires `pg_advisory_xact_lock(hashtext('operator_slots:' || subaccount_id))`, then runs the count, then inserts the chain-link row. The lock is released at COMMIT. `SELECT count(*) ... FOR UPDATE` is insufficient on its own because aggregate counts do not lock the absence of rows.
626:   - **New user-requested operator task over the cap:** REJECTED at task-create / first-dispatch with typed error `OPERATOR_SESSION_LIMIT_EXCEEDED`. Customer-facing message surfaced via the existing task-create / operator-capacity modal (canonical component path chosen by the implementation chunk; the mockup `r8-modal-concurrency-limit.html` documents the intended pattern). NOT queued. NOT an incident.
627:   - **Existing chain-continuation hitting the cap mid-task:** QUEUED FIFO on the new `'operator-session-dispatch-next-chain-link'` pg-boss queue. Task state stays `paused_for_chain_continuation`. Dispatched when a slot frees. NOT an incident — normal flow control.
629:   **Slot-free wake-up mechanism.** After every chain-link finalise (terminal `completed | failed | cancelled`), the finaliser calls `operatorChainSchedulerService.releaseSlotAndEnqueueNext(subaccountId)`. Under the same `pg_advisory_xact_lock(hashtext('operator_slots:' || subaccount_id))` used at dispatch (§ 7.1 step 3), the scheduler scans the oldest `paused_for_chain_continuation` task for that subaccount whose pending `'operator-session-dispatch-next-chain-link'` job has been throttled by the cap, and enqueues exactly one new dispatch job for the freed slot. If multiple tasks are queued, the FIFO order is `agent_runs.updated_at ASC` for tasks in `paused_for_chain_continuation`. The pure helper for the scan/order lives in `operatorChainSchedulerServicePure.ts` (§ 5.1) and is unit-tested per § 12.

840:**Namespace discipline.** Hyphenated namespace for lifecycle events: `operator-session.*`. The `operator.*` namespace is reserved for INCIDENT and system-monitoring events (§ 4.8). Audit events live under existing audit namespaces (`task.operator.*`, `subaccount.operator_settings.*`) and ride the existing audit primitives (§ 4.9) — they do NOT use the `operator.*` reservation. Any new lifecycle event MUST register in `shared/types/operatorBackendEvents.ts` (a new file) which is the single source of truth for the discriminated union. A CI gate (`verify-operator-event-registry.sh`) checks for naked string literals matching the family pattern outside the registry.
846:**Producer:** the adapter's `dispatch()` path on every failed attempt (1st, 2nd, 3rd). **Consumer:** the system-monitoring agent via `recordIncident()` → `system-monitor-ingest` queue.
852:### 4.8b CS notification event (`cs.operator_session.suspended_detected`)
854:Single typed CS notification introduced by this spec. Produced by `notifyOperatorSessionSuspended()` (`server/services/operatorSessionSuspensionNotifier.ts`, § 5.1) and consumed by the existing inbox pipeline.
876:**Idempotency key:** `(connection_id, usability_state, detection_date)` — at most one CS notification per connection per state per day. `detection_date` is derived from the persisted broker `usability_state` transition timestamp (the broker stamps the row at the transition; the notifier reads that stamp, not its own call time). This guarantees a stable key across retries of the same notifier invocation.
878:**Consumer:** existing inbox / notification pipeline. No new pipeline component is introduced.
891:All audit events flow through the existing `securityAuditService` writer or its task-action sibling. The implementation chunk picks the correct writer per event family; no new audit primitive is introduced.
937:**New typed columns vs `metadata` jsonb.** Only two columns are added to `llm_requests` by this spec: `operator_run_id` (nullable; references `operator_runs(id)`) and `boundary` (nullable; the discriminator the cost-writer keys on — currently the single value `'chain_link'`). The other operator-specific fields in the example rows above (`chain_seq`, `vendor_session_id`, `credential_mode`, `plan_tier`, `step_count`, `vcpu_seconds`, `wall_clock_ms`, `peak_memory_bytes`) are written into the existing `llm_requests.metadata` jsonb column, NOT as new typed columns. The cost-writer's JSON shape is named in `operatorCostWriterPure.ts` (§ 5.1). Migration `0331` also adds the covering index `(operator_run_id)` for cost-writer idempotency lookups and the partial UNIQUE `(operator_run_id, source_type, boundary)`.

1118:### 6.5b Backend route guards for the new task-action routes
1120:All routes in `server/routes/operatorTasks.ts` (§ 5.1) MUST mount under `authenticate`, resolve the agent run + subaccount, call `setOrgGUC()`, and enforce a route-specific actor rule before mutating state. Actor rules match § 6.6 UI gates:
1122:| Route | Actor rule | Permission key |
1130:The `manager+` / assigned-user rule is enforced in the route handler (not by a single permission key) because the underlying state transitions are user-initiated lifecycle actions, not admin operations. The route handler reads `agent_runs.assigned_user_id` and `users.role` before authorising.
1132:### 6.6 UI permission gates
1147:2. **No cross-tenant adapter calls** — `operatorManagedBackend.dispatch()` reads `agent_runs.subaccount_id` once, sets the GUC via `setOrgGUC()`, and uses the same scoped tx for every subsequent read/write within the chain link.
1149:4. **The pg-boss handlers re-read** the org/subaccount from the row they're processing and re-establish the GUC before any tenant-scoped write (the queue payload carries `operator_run_id`; the handler resolves the rest).
1150:5. **The polling route** subaccount-checks via `setOrgGUC` + `getOrgScopedDb`; a row whose `subaccount_id` doesn't match the caller's principal returns 404 (NOT 403, to avoid leaking existence — consistent with the existing IEE route).
1161:2. Set the GUC; resolve effective caps (`subaccountOperatorSettingsService.getEffectiveSettings(subaccountId)`).
1162:3. Concurrency-cap check. Acquire `pg_advisory_xact_lock(hashtext('operator_slots:' || subaccount_id))` inside the dispatch tx; then `count(*) FROM operator_runs WHERE subaccount_id=$1 AND status='running' AND superseded_by_attempt IS NULL`; then proceed with the `operator_runs` INSERT under the same lock (released at COMMIT). Plain `SELECT ... FOR UPDATE` is insufficient — aggregate counts do not lock absent rows (§ 10.3). If new task hitting cap → throw `OPERATOR_SESSION_LIMIT_EXCEEDED` (NOT queued, per § 3.17 item 5). If chain-continuation hitting cap → return a structured response that the chain-resume dispatcher handles by re-queueing (FIFO).
1164:5. Resolve credential via `credentialBrokerService.requestOperatorSessionCredential` (or `resolveFallback` if stickiness is set).
1165:6. Resolve / create profile via `operatorTaskProfileService.ensureActiveProfile(taskId, attemptNumber)`.
1167:8. Call `sandboxExecutionService.runTask(...)` to start the sandbox session, injecting the credential and mounting the profile. The call MUST pass a `sandbox_start_key = operator_run_id` provider-side idempotency token so the sandbox provider can reject a duplicate start. The sandbox-isolation primitive supports this per Spec B.
1173:1. Re-read the row; if `status='pending'` AND `vendor_session_id IS NULL`, call `sandboxExecutionService.adoptOrStart({ sandbox_start_key: operator_run_id, ... })` (the sandbox primitive returns the existing sandbox if one was created under that token, otherwise starts a fresh one).
1181:### 7.2 Chain-link terminal event — queued (pg-boss)
1183:When the sandbox session terminates (operator runtime emits a terminal step-state OR hard cap is reached OR cancel propagated OR runtime crashed), the adapter writes the chain-link row to its terminal status and enqueues `'operator-session-completed'` with payload `{ operatorRunId, agentRunId }`.
1185:The handler `operatorSessionCompletedHandler.ts`:
1191:5. If paused-for-continuation: parent agent run sets `status='paused_for_chain_continuation'`; cost rows for THIS chain link are written via the same writer (per-chain-link cost rows happen regardless of pause/terminal); the chain-resume dispatcher enqueues `'operator-session-dispatch-next-chain-link'` with payload `{ agentRunId }`.
1193:**Idempotency posture (per § 10.1):** key-based on `(operator_run_id, status)`. A re-delivery of the queue message is a no-op — the finaliser sees the row already in terminal state and returns the prior result.
1195:### 7.3 Chain-link dispatch — queued (pg-boss) with backoff retry
1197:`operatorSessionDispatchNextChainLinkHandler.ts`:
1201:   - `agent_runs.status` is one of `'pending'` (first dispatch — bootstrap path), `'paused_for_chain_continuation'`, `'paused_chain_failure'` (after user-initiated retry, counter has been reset), or `'paused_budget_exceeded'` (after user-initiated extension). NOTE: `'delegated'` is intentionally excluded — a `'delegated'` task already has a chain link in flight, and dispatching another would race.
1202:   - The queued-job reason tag matches the current paused-state resume action (`'continuation'` ↔ `paused_for_chain_continuation`; `'retry'` ↔ `paused_chain_failure`; `'budget_extension'` ↔ `paused_budget_exceeded`; `'bootstrap'` ↔ `pending`).
1206:4. On success: writes `agent_runs.status='delegated'` via the optimistic predicate `UPDATE agent_runs SET status='delegated', operator_chain_failure_count=0 WHERE id=$1 AND status IN ('pending','delegated','paused_for_chain_continuation','paused_chain_failure','paused_budget_exceeded')`. 0 rows-affected means the task is in a terminal state — no-op.
1207:5. On failure with `'transient'` failure class: increments `agent_runs.operator_chain_failure_count` (per § 3.4 writer rules — predicate `UPDATE ... WHERE status IN ('delegated','paused_for_chain_continuation')`); enqueues a delayed re-dispatch (1 min → 5 min → 15 min via pg-boss's `startAfter` parameter).
1208:6. On the 3rd consecutive failure: writes `agent_runs.status='paused_chain_failure'`, emits `'operator-session.task_paused_chain_failure'` event, sends user notification.
1212:**Idempotency posture:** key-based on `(agentRunId, attempt_number, chain_seq_next)`. `chain_seq_next` is computed as `max(chain_seq) + 1` **within the current `attempt_number`** (NOT across attempts — fresh-profile restart restarts chain_seq at 1 for the new attempt per § 3.15 item 7). Re-delivery of the queue message is a no-op when the chain link is already in `pending`/`running`/terminal state at that `(attempt_number, chain_seq_next)`.
1214:### 7.4 Progress events — queued (pg-boss) + WebSocket bridge
1216:Step-boundary events from the operator runtime are enqueued (`'operator-session-progressed'`) to keep the runtime's hot path off the DB. `operatorSessionProgressedHandler.ts` is the **sole writer** for `operator_runs.last_progress_at` and `step_count`:
1219:2. If step 1 updated 0 rows: log the drop and return (no WebSocket emission). Otherwise emit `'operator-session.progressed'` to the `agent-run:{runId}` WebSocket room via `emitAgentRunUpdate`.
1221:The WebSocket bridge is best-effort: a dropped event is acceptable (the next event picks up the state). The polling fallback route is the durable visibility path.
1223:### 7.5 Profile GC — queued (pg-boss cron)
1225:`operatorTaskProfileGcHandler.ts` is a 15-minute cron job that scans for `(status='scheduled_gc' AND scheduled_gc_at <= now())` rows, marks them `'gc_in_progress'`, deletes the underlying sandbox volume via the sandbox provider, then sets `'gc_done'`. The scan is system-wide.
1227:`operator_task_profiles` has `FORCE ROW LEVEL SECURITY` (§ 6.2), so the cron CANNOT use the default `db` handle (it would fail-closed with 0 rows on every UPDATE — the same pattern as `workflowDraftsCleanupJob`, `llmLedgerArchiveJob`, and the agent-run cleanup job). The handler MUST follow the existing cross-org maintenance pattern from `architecture.md` § *Row-Level Security — Three-Layer Fail-Closed Data Isolation* / § *Admin-bypass RLS*:
1230:await withAdminConnection({ source: 'operatorTaskProfileGc' }, async (tx) => {
1236:`admin_role` carries `BYPASSRLS`; every invocation is logged to `audit_events` by `withAdminConnection`.
1240:**Stale `'gc_in_progress'` reclaim.** A crash during volume deletion can strand a row in `'gc_in_progress'` forever. `operator_task_profiles` includes `gc_started_at timestamptz NULL` (set when the row transitions to `'gc_in_progress'`, cleared on transition to `'gc_done'`). The GC handler reclaims any row where `status='gc_in_progress' AND gc_started_at < now() - INTERVAL '30 minutes'` by treating it as eligible for a fresh deletion attempt. Provider HTTP 404 on the delete call is treated as success (volume already gone) and transitions the row to `'gc_done'`.
1244:The cost-writer is **NOT a separate queue**. It runs inline within the `finalise()` transaction triggered by `'operator-session-completed'`. The terminal `status` on `operator_runs` was written by the adapter at chain-link end (§ 7.2). The finaliser does NOT re-set the terminal status; it commits the cost rows together with stamping `operator_runs.event_emitted_at = now()` so that "cost rows written" and "terminal event acknowledged" land atomically. This avoids the "event acknowledged but no cost row" or "cost row but event still un-acknowledged" partial state.
1246:If the cost-writer fails inside the finaliser: the transaction rolls back, `event_emitted_at` stays NULL, and the pg-boss queue retries delivery. The cost-writer's own idempotency (key-based on `(operator_run_id, source_type, boundary)`) ensures the retry doesn't double-write. The chain-link `status` itself was already committed by the adapter and is not affected by the rollback.
1272:1. **No backward dependency.** Every column referenced by code in Chunk N is created in an equal-or-earlier chunk's migration. Verified via the dependency table in § 14.
1276:The implementation order is: schemas + migrations FIRST, then services FIRST among code, then routes, then UI, then renames + CS runbook + ADR + CI gates. Specific chunk ordering is in § 14.
1286:| `agent_runs` terminal UPDATE to `completed` or `failed` | **state-based** | optimistic predicate: `UPDATE ... WHERE status='delegated'`. A paused task MUST transition `delegated` first (re-dispatch a chain link) before it can roll up to terminal `completed`/`failed`. 0 rows-affected = already terminal OR still paused; finaliser logs and returns 200 idempotent-hit. |
1287:| `agent_runs` terminal UPDATE to `cancelled` | **state-based** | optimistic predicate: `UPDATE ... WHERE status IN ('pending','delegated','paused_for_chain_continuation','paused_chain_failure','paused_budget_exceeded')`. Any pre-terminal state may transition directly to `cancelled` (user cancel). 0 rows-affected = already terminal; return `409` with current state. |
1288:| `agent_runs` pause UPDATE (`paused_for_chain_continuation`) | **state-based** | optimistic predicate: `UPDATE ... WHERE status='delegated'`. 0 rows-affected = a concurrent path already paused or terminated. |
1291:| `operator_runs` progress UPDATE (`last_progress_at`, `step_count`) | **key-based** | event key `(operator_run_id, step_index)`; the handler uses `greatest(last_progress_at, ...)` and `greatest(step_count, ...)` so duplicate / out-of-order deliveries are no-ops. The pg-boss enqueue carries the same singleton key. |
1292:| `llm_requests` cost rows | **key-based** | unique index: `(operator_run_id, source_type, boundary)` for the new rows (added by migration `0331`); existing `(agent_run_id, request_id)` for `per_token` rows. 23505 → idempotent-hit. |
1293:| pg-boss `'operator-session-completed'` enqueue | **key-based** | pg-boss singleton key: `'operator-session-completed:' || operator_run_id`. Re-enqueue is a no-op. |
1294:| pg-boss `'operator-session-dispatch-next-chain-link'` enqueue | **key-based** | singleton key: `'operator-session-dispatch-next-chain-link:' || agent_run_id || ':' || attempt_number || ':' || chain_seq_next`. |
1295:| pg-boss `'operator-task-profile-gc'` cron tick | **state-based** | the cron handler's `UPDATE WHERE status='scheduled_gc' AND scheduled_gc_at <= now() RETURNING id` is the eligibility predicate; concurrent ticks see disjoint row sets. |
1302:| `credentialBrokerService.requestOperatorSessionCredential` | **guarded** | broker enforces its own idempotency; safe to retry on network errors. |
1303:| `sandboxExecutionService.runTask` | **guarded** | the `sandbox_start_key = operator_run_id` token (§ 7.1) gives the provider exactly-once semantics. On retry: `sandboxExecutionService.adoptOrStart()` either adopts the existing sandbox under the token or starts a fresh one. Without the token a retry would orphan the prior sandbox. |
1306:| WebSocket emission `emitAgentRunUpdate` | **safe** | best-effort; loss is acceptable. |
1307:| `operatorSessionDispatchNextChainLinkHandler` | **guarded** | wrapped by `operator_runs` (chain_seq) idempotency. |
1308:| `operatorTaskProfileGcHandler` | **guarded** | row-state predicate prevents double-delete. |
1317:| Two concurrent dispatches racing past the concurrency cap | `pg_advisory_xact_lock(hashtext('operator_slots:' || subaccount_id))` inside the dispatch tx; the lock serialises all dispatchers for the same subaccount. The count then runs against `operator_runs WHERE subaccount_id=$1 AND status='running' AND superseded_by_attempt IS NULL`. The lock is released at COMMIT. Plain `SELECT count(*) FOR UPDATE` is insufficient — aggregate counts don't lock absent rows. |
1321:| Fresh-profile-restart racing in-flight chain link | the restart route requires the task to be in a paused state. Optimistic predicate: `UPDATE agent_runs SET ... WHERE status IN ('paused_chain_failure','paused_budget_exceeded','paused_for_chain_continuation')`. Terminal `failed | completed | cancelled` is never restarted under the same `agent_run_id` (§ 10.7 forbidden transitions). A `running`/`delegated` chain link blocks restart. |
1328:- Post-terminal prohibition: no further events with the same `chain_link_id` after a terminal event. **Exception:** `'operator-session.artefact_harvested'` (§ 4.7) is allowed to fire AFTER the chain-link terminal event only because artefact harvest can complete asynchronously to the chain-link finalise. When `artefact_harvested` fires post-terminal, its payload MUST omit `chain_link_id` and reference the task by `agent_run_id` only. When it fires pre-terminal (the common case), it carries `chain_link_id`. The harvest writer decides which form based on whether the chain link is still `'running'` at harvest time.
1336:- **Single-writer guard.** Before emitting any `operator-session.task_*` terminal event, the writer MUST acquire the singleton key `operator-session-task-terminal:${agent_run_id}` (via pg-boss singleton enqueue OR via an `INSERT INTO task_terminal_event_guard (agent_run_id) ON CONFLICT DO NOTHING RETURNING ...` write — implementation chunk picks one mechanism). The first writer that acquires the key emits; subsequent writers (e.g. a racing finaliser after a user cancel won the `agent_runs` UPDATE) see the conflict and no-op. This guarantees exactly one task-terminal event per task even when cancel and finaliser race.
1352:| `operator_task_profiles (task_id, attempt_number) UNIQUE` | Concurrent ensure-profile | 23505 caught, idempotent-hit, returns existing row body to caller. (Internal route's HTTP equivalent: 200 idempotent.) |
1360:No `23505` is allowed to bubble as a 500. The typed exception classes — `OperatorBackendConflictError` for 409 cases and `OperatorSessionLimitExceededError` for 429 — live in `server/services/operatorBackendErrors.ts` (§ 5.1). They are mapped to the HTTP statuses above by the existing route error-handler middleware (the same one already mapping `ZodError` and the other typed-error classes); the build chunk wires the case clauses, no new mapper file is introduced.
1374:running → cancelled        (user cancelled mid-link OR task-level cancel propagated)
1387:pending → delegated                                  (first chain dispatch)
1388:delegated → paused_for_chain_continuation            (chain link completed with checkpoint, task not done)
1389:paused_for_chain_continuation → delegated            (next chain link dispatched)
1390:delegated → paused_chain_failure                     (3 consecutive dispatch failures)
1391:paused_chain_failure → delegated                     (user retried)
1392:delegated → paused_budget_exceeded                   (budget cap hit)
1393:paused_budget_exceeded → delegated                   (user extended budget)
1394:delegated → completed                                (final chain link task_completed)
1395:delegated → failed                                   (operator runtime hard error OR max chain length)
1396:delegated → paused_chain_failure                     (hard-cap unresumable: running chain link with failed_mid_step=true per § 3.14 item 3; counted in the same dispatch-failure budget as start failures)
1397:{pending | delegated | paused_*} → cancelled         (user cancelled)
1402:- `pending → completed | failed` without going through `delegated` (operator-managed tasks must enter delegation first before completion or failure). **`pending → cancelled` IS permitted** — a user may cancel a task before its first chain-link dispatch.
1403:- `paused_* → completed | failed` without re-entering `delegated` (a paused task MUST resume to dispatch a chain link before it can produce a task-terminal `completed`/`failed` status). **`paused_* → cancelled` IS permitted** at any time (user cancel from a paused state).
